Exit Site
If you are in danger, call 911. If you need to exit this website quickly, click on the ESCAPE button. This button will immediately open a browser window for weather.com and replace your current window with google.com.

## The .gov means it's official. 
Local, state, and federal government websites often end in .gov. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania government websites and email systems use "pennsylvania.gov" or "pa.gov" at the end of the address. Before sharing sensitive or personal information, make sure you're on an official state website.

M I S S I O N S T A T E M E N T To promote healthy behaviors, p revent injury and disease, and to assure the safe delivery of quality health care for all people in Pennsylvania. Page 1 of 307Page 1 of 307
* * *
## Pennsylvania Department of Health
State Fiscal Year 2026-27 Recommended Budget NarraƟve Statement The mission of the Department of Health (DOH) is to promote healthy behaviors, prevent injury and disease, and to ensure the safe delivery of quality health care for all people in Pennsylvania. To accomplish this mission, th e department works collaboraƟvely with public and private community partners to facilitate the development of an eﬀecƟve public health system. The department licenses and regulates a variety of health faciliƟes, monitors health outcomes, and provides outreach, educaƟon, prevenƟon, and treatment services. Community-based groups receive grants to provide essen Ɵal services to the Commonwealth’s residents including programs to support family health, nutri Ɵon, immunizaƟon, diagnosis and treatment of certain blood and communicable diseases, and cancer control and prevenƟon. Programs and Goals Health Support Services: To provide eﬀecƟve administraƟon and support systems through which the substan Ɵve programs of the health delivery system and the department can be achieved. Health Research: To enha nce the basic scienƟﬁc knowledge of the nature of disease, illness, and the environment, which will improve the use of exisƟng and new health resources. PrevenƟ ve Health: To reduce morbidity and mortality through the early detecƟon of disease and health defects and the promoƟon of prevenƟve health pracƟces and remedial care. Health Treatment Services: To ma ximize the individual’s capacity for independent living through the provision of an array of service and support programs. The 2026-27 Recommended Budget for the Department of Health re ﬂects the Department’s eﬀorts to responsibly manage available resources to areas of greatest need. This document exhibits the Department’s goal to deliver program services to the public in the most e ﬃcient and eﬀecƟve manner. Funding for state complement has been requested for ﬁlled posiƟons and current year authorized adjustments. Filled posi Ɵons are budgeted at 26.1 pay periods. Vacant posiƟons are funded at 9 pay periods. AppropriaƟons Highlights Fund 10497 – General Government OperaƟons – Reﬂects an increase of $3.351 million from the SFY2025 Enacted Budget. $2.019 of this increase is to maintain the Pennsylvania Immuniza Ɵon Electronic Registry System. The remaining increase is to sustain current programs with inﬂaƟonary increases. Fund 11198 – Health PromoƟon and Disease PrevenƟon – Reﬂects an increase of $2.500 million from the SFY2025 Enacted Budget and three new posiƟons to expand support for maternal health programs. Fund 10471 – St ate Health Care Centers – Reﬂects an increase of $2.231 million from the SFY2025 Enacted Budget due to increases in informa Ɵon technology costs, personnel costs, annual leases, and travel related costs due to requirements to increase onsite collaboraƟons and visits across the state. Fund 10467 – Qu ality Assurance – Reﬂects an increase of $1.859 million from the SFY2025 Enacted Budget. This is mainly for the SoŌware as a Service (SaaS) that supports quality assurance. Fund 10470 – State Laboratory – Reﬂects an increase of $1.297 million from the SFY2025 Enacted Budget. This is mainly due to a criƟcal need to replace aging laboratory equipment and increased operaƟng costs due to inﬂaƟon. Page 2 of 307Page 2 of 307

The Fiscal Year 2026-2027 Governor's Executive Budget reflects an increase of $3.351 million in state funds from the Fiscal Year 2025-2026 funding level of $32.057 million. ## General Government OperaƟons
The General Government Opera Ɵons appropria Ɵon provides funding to support the general management and infrastructure for operaƟon of public health programs. Included in this appropriaƟon are the salary and opera Ɵonal funds to support: the O ﬃce of the Secretary; the execuƟve funcƟons of the Deputy Secretaries; and the Oﬃces of CommunicaƟons, Chief Counsel, OperaƟonal Excellence (OpEx), Policy, Budget, Procurement, and LegislaƟve Aﬀairs.
* * *
Oﬃce of the Secretary The Secretary of Health (SOH) dire cts and supervises the administra Ɵon of the Department and establishes policy and direcƟon for the state’s public health programs.
* * *
Oﬃce of AdministraƟon The Deputy Secretary for AdministraƟon serves as an advisor to the SOH on departmental administraƟve ma Ʃers and oversees the Procurement O ﬃce, as well as being the liaison for Human Resources (HR) and InformaƟon Technology (IT).
* * *
Oﬃce of the ExecuƟve Deputy Secretary The ExecuƟve Deputy Secretary serves as an advisor to the SOH and oversees the Oﬃces of the Deputy Secretaries in addiƟon to OpEx, Bureau of Medical Marijuana, and Long-Term Care TransformaƟon Oﬃce.
* * *
Oﬃce of Health Preparedness and Community ProtecƟon The Deputate for Health Preparedness and Community ProtecƟon oversees a wide range of public health work under the Bureau of Community Health Systems, Bureau of Emergency Preparedness and Response, Bureau of Epidemiology, Bureau of Laboratories, Bureau of Emergency Medical Services, and the COVID-19 Response and Recovery team. The Deputate provides direc Ɵon for statewide public health planning and response; collects and interprets surveillance data; responds to exis Ɵng and emer ging health threats; provides public health laboratory tesƟng; oversees the state EMS system; and provides direct clinical care through State Health Centers. The Deputate receives signi ﬁcant federal funding to carry out public health acƟviƟes.
* * *
Oﬃce of Quality Assurance The Deputate for Quality Assurance assures compliance with federal and state regulaƟons, ensuring quality of care in various health care facili Ɵes, including but not limited to hospitals, ambulatory surgical centers, nursing care faciliƟes, home health agencies, and hospices.
* * *
Page 18 of 307Page 18 of 307
* * *
## Oﬃce of Health PromoƟon and Disease PrevenƟon
Health Promo Ɵon and Disease Preven Ɵon oversees the work of ﬁve bureaus in the Department. The Bureau of Communicable Diseases focuses on work with HIV, sexually transmiƩed diseases, and tuberculosis. The Bureau of Family Health’s mission is to equally protect and promote the health and well-being of pregnant people, their partners, their children, and all families through newborn screening, child and adult health speci ﬁc programs, and the Maternal Mortality Review CommiƩee. The Bureau of Health PromoƟon and Risk PrevenƟon oversees work in nutriƟon and physical acƟvity, tobacco prevenƟon and control, cancer prevenƟon and control, and violence preven Ɵon programming. The Bureau of Immuniza Ɵons provides educa Ɵon and access to vaccines throughout the lifespan. Finally, the Bureau of Women, Infants, and Children (WIC) focuses on nutri Ɵon, educa Ɵon, breas ƞeeding support, health care and social service referrals for children, pregnant women, mothers, and caregivers.
* * *
Oﬃce of Health Resources and Services The Deputate of Health Resources and Services oversees the Bureau of Health Sta ƟsƟcs and Registries and the O ﬃces of Health Research, Pennsylvania Primary Care, and Drug Surveillance and Misuse PrevenƟon.
* * *
Oﬃce of OperaƟonal Excellence The OpEx strategizes, coordinates, and directs the ac ƟviƟes of the departmental plans, including the Strategic Plan, the State Health Assessment, the State Health Improvement Plan, the Quality Improvement Plan, and its linkages to the Performance Management System. OpEx directs the coordina Ɵon of maintaining Public Health Accredita Ɵon, coordinates and leads Enterprise Risk Management acƟviƟes, and oversees the acƟviƟes of the Health Equity Oﬃce.
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons

WIC AdministraƟon & OperaƟon All administrative costs associated with the WIC Program are in this appropriation.
* * *
Health Assessment The purpose of the program is to rapidly iden Ɵfy and miƟgate the environmental health hazards associated with hazardous waste sites listed, or proposed for lis Ɵng, on the U.S. Environmental Protec Ɵon Agency’s (EPA) Na Ɵonal Priority List (NPL), and other types of hazardous waste sites idenƟﬁed by the Department of Environmental ProtecƟon (DEP), or acƟve industries potenƟally impacƟng the health of nearby communiƟes. The Commonwealth has 91 hazardous waste sites listed, or proposed for lisƟng, on the NPL, which is the third most sites for a state. The poten Ɵal for chemical contamina Ɵon of soil, air, and water is not limited to communiƟes surrounding NPL sites. ScaƩered across Pennsylvania, in urban, suburban, and rural communiƟes, there are numerous historical and current industries that are potenƟal sources of Page 19 of 307Page 19 of 307
* * *
environmental contamina Ɵon. Examples include steel produc Ɵon, mining and smel Ɵng, oil reﬁning, oil and natural gas opera Ɵons, and agriculture, as well as Hazardous Sites Cleanup Act locaƟons, landﬁlls, responsible party/NPL deferral sites, and formerly used defense sites. Through the Coopera Ɵve Agreement with the federal Agency for Toxic Substances and Disease Registry's (ATSDR) Partnership to Promote Local E ﬀorts to Reduce Environmental Exposure, the Department conducts health assessments and consulta Ɵons, site reviews and updates, and in-person community health educaƟon and public meeƟngs on the NPL or non-NPL sites. These assessments include: an evalua Ɵon of data on the release of hazardous substances into the environment to assess adverse impacts on public health; development of health advisories or other public health recommenda Ɵons; and iden ƟﬁcaƟon of studies or ac Ɵons needed to evaluate, prevent, or miƟgate human health eﬀects. The health assessment team hosts community outreach and educa Ɵon events, such as soil screening, health, outreach, and partnership (soilSHOP). At a soilSHOP event, re sidents can bring soil samples for heavy metal screening, receive health educaƟon on heavy metal exposures from soil in gardens and play areas, safe gardening Ɵps, and ways to reduce harmful exposures. AddiƟonally, this program evaluates current and proposed early care and educa Ɵon sites based on the informa Ɵon collected from providers via a voluntary online survey. This helps ensure that children a Ʃending these faciliƟes are not exposed to any known and/or poten Ɵal environmental hazards. It also funds grant acƟviƟes that include traveling to sites, conduc Ɵng community health educa Ɵon and outreach, and parƟcipaƟng in public meeƟngs hosted by DOH, DEP, ATSDR, EPA, and/or other agencies.
* * *
PHHSBG – AdministraƟon & OperaƟon This appropria Ɵon funds personnel and opera Ɵng c osts for the Preven Ɵve Health and Health Services Block Grant. Federal block grant statutory requirements restrict administra Ɵon funding to 10% of the total award. This appropria Ɵon funds personnel and opera Ɵng expenses for staﬀ involved in the administra Ɵon of heart disease and stroke; child, adolescent, and adult obesity; injury and violence preven Ɵon; oral health; chronic disease health educa Ɵon and promoƟon; and other educaƟonal and community-based prevenƟve health programs.
* * *
MCHSBG – AdministraƟon & OperaƟon This appropriaƟon supports the administraƟon of programs funded by the Maternal and Child Health Services Block Grant. It supports all maternal and child health programs for acƟviƟes such as infrastructure, program development, program monitoring, technical assistance, and mechanisms for accountability in all maternal and child health programs. Federal restric Ɵons require that no more than 10% of the grant award be uƟlized for administraƟve purposes.
* * *
Emergency Medical Services for Children This funding is to administer and support Pennsylvania’s Emergency Medical Services for Children (EMSC) State Partnership Program dedicated to improving emergency care for children in both illness and injury across the conƟnuum of emergency care. ## Tuberculosis Program – AdministraƟon and OperaƟon
This appropria Ɵon funds ac ƟviƟes to prevent transmission of and prevent progression from latent TB infecƟon to acƟve TB disease by diagnosis/treatment of persons with TB disease and persons with latent TB infec Ɵon (LTBI); examinaƟon of immigrants and refugees; targeted tesƟng for, and treatment of, LTBI; program planning, evalua Ɵon, and improvement; epidemiologic surveillance and response; HR development and partnership acƟviƟes; and public health laboratory strengthening.
* * *
Lead – AdministraƟon and OperaƟon The Department receives funding from Ho using and Urban Development (HUD) and the Centers for Disease Control and Preven Ɵon (CDC) to administer lead hazard control grants that focus on primary and secondary lead exposure preven Ɵon and educa Ɵon. This funding covers the administraƟve and operaƟonal costs of HUD’s lead-based paint hazard control program and CDC’s childhood lead poisoning prevenƟon program.
* * *
AIDS Health EducaƟon Program This fund provides AIDS health educaƟon and other services to increase public awareness of AIDS-related issues and prevenƟon measures.
* * *
Primary Care CooperaƟve Agreement This grant facilitates planning and coordinaƟon of primary care strategies between state and federal governments, while fostering connecƟon with community-based primary providers. The objecƟve is to enhance the availability of primary care services for medically underserved ciƟzens in Pennsylvania. The grant supports the iden ƟﬁcaƟon and federal designa Ɵon of health professional shortage areas (HPSAs) and medically underserved areas (MUAs). Once designated, health care providers in these regions may become eligible for federal and state programs aimed at improving pracƟƟoner recruitment and retenƟon. Furthermore, the grant assists in qualifying pracƟce sit es for par ƟcipaƟon in the NaƟonal Health Service Corps, a federal iniƟaƟve focused on the recruitment and retenƟon of primary health care providers in underserved communiƟes.
* * *
HIV/AIDS Surveillance This program systemaƟcally collects, analyzes, and interprets HIV data in Pennsylvania to characterize trends in HIV infec Ɵon and detect ac Ɵve HIV transmission to advance implementaƟon of appropriate public health interven Ɵons. Supplementary ac ƟviƟes implemented include the Medical Monitoring Project (MMP), data-to-care, and detec Ɵon and monitoring of HIV transmission clusters. The MMP is a surveillance system designed to learn more about the experiences and needs of people who are living with HIV. MMP is important because it provides informaƟon about the behaviors, medical care, an d health status of people living with HIV. MMP is unique in that it describes co mprehensive clinical and behavioral informaƟon from persons carefully sampled to represent everyone diagnosed with HIV in the United States. Page 21 of 307Page 21 of 307
* * *
Because MMP’s esƟmates are designed to be representa Ɵve, informaƟon gathered from MMP may be used by preven Ɵon planning groups, policy leaders, health care providers, and people living with HIV to highlight dispariƟes in care and services and advocate for needed resources.
* * *
HIV Care – AdministraƟon and OperaƟon This program provides formula-based ﬁnancial assistance to states, and certain high incidence ciƟes, for the AIDS Drug Assistance Program (ADAP)/Special Pharmaceu Ɵcal Beneﬁts Program (SPBP) for people living with HIV (PLWH) who meet certain eligibility criteria and are not eligible for pharmaceu Ɵcals under Medical Assistance (MA) programs. This appropria Ɵon provides funding for laboratory services, HIV anƟretroviral medicaƟons, drugs used to treat life threatening opportunis Ɵc infec Ɵons, and other medica Ɵons to support the overall health of enrolled PLWH. This is accomplished through heal th insurance premium assistance for enrolled clients or full payment. Matching funds of one dollar of state funds for every two dollars of federal funds is provided through AIDS Programs and Special Pharmaceu Ɵcal Services. This program provides formula-based ﬁnancial assistance to states, and certain high-incidence ciƟes, to enable them to improve the quality, availability, and organizaƟon of health care and support services for individuals living with HIV and their families. This is accomplished, in part, through the funding of regional HIV grantees, inclusive of the Philadelphia Department of Public Health, that covers the enƟre state. Grantees enter into agreements for a comprehensive con Ɵnuum of medical and support services needed for individuals living wi th HIV and their families. These funds are used as payor of last resort; therefore, HIV rebate funds acquired through the 340b program are used ﬁrst to support the provision of these HIV care support services. The grantees and their sub grantees are responsible for repor Ɵng informaƟon regarding client demographics and services provided. This informa Ɵon is used at agency, regional, and statewide levels for planning and reporƟng purposes. The data collected are elements iden Ɵﬁed by the Health Resource and Services AdministraƟon (HRSA).
* * *
Cancer PrevenƟon & Control The Cancer PrevenƟon and Control focuses on decreasing cancer incidence and morbidity by using da ta to assess the cancer burden and inform program planning and implementa Ɵon of evidence-based interven Ɵons. It supports the Statewide PA Cancer Coali Ɵon and the implementaƟon of the 2023-33 Cancer Plan. It con Ɵnues to provide quality breast and cervical cancer screenings and diagnos Ɵcs to low-income uninsured and underinsured females and supports health and wellness in cancer survivors.
* * *
Pennsylvania’s Cancer PrevenƟon and Control ConƟnuum of Care CollaboraƟve These funds are categorized within three components. The Na Ɵonal Comprehensive Cancer Control Program supports an acƟve cancer coaliƟon of stakeholders across Pennsylvania and assists the Department with the development, implementa Ɵon, and evalua Ɵon of Pennsylvania’s Comprehensive Cancer Contro l Plan. The plan contains goals, objec Ɵves and Page 22 of 307Page 22 of 307
* * *
strategies to address the public health needs for disparate popula Ɵons across the conƟnuum of cancer care, with the goal of reducing cancer incidence in the Commonwealth. The Na Ɵonal Breast and Cervical Cancer Early Detec Ɵon Program supports statewide comprehensive breast and cervical cancer screening, and the PA Breast and Cervical Cancer Early DetecƟon Program. The purpose of the program is to provide breast and cervical cancer screening services for underserved women. Women ages 21 to 64 with low/moderate incomes who are uninsured or underinsured are eligible for the program. The Pennsylvania Cancer Registry (PCR) is Pennsylvania's statewide popula Ɵon-based cancer incidence registry, as mandated by the Pennsylvania Cancer Control, Preven Ɵon, and Research Act and disease repor Ɵng regula Ɵons in SecƟon 27.31 of 28 Pa Code Chapter 27 (Communicable and Noncommunicable Diseases). Located within the Bureau of Health StaƟsƟcs and Registries, the PCR has been collecƟ ng informa Ɵon about all cancers diagnosed in Pennsylvania (except basal and squamous cell carcinoma of the skin and carcinoma in situ of the cervix) since 1985. The PCR co llects demographic, diagnosƟc, and treatment informa Ɵon on all paƟents diagnosed and treated at hospitals, laboratories, other healthcare facili Ɵes, and health care pracƟƟoners’ oﬃces in Pennsylvania. The PCR is design ed to monitor cancer trends over Ɵme; determine cancer paƩerns in various populaƟons; guide planning and evaluaƟon of cancer control programs to determine whether prevenƟon, screening, and treatment eﬀorts are making a di ﬀerence; help set priori Ɵes for alloca Ɵng health resources; and advance clinical, epidemiological, and health services research. Since 1994, the PCR has par Ɵcipated in the NaƟonal Program of Cancer Registries administered by the CDC. Through this program, CDC provides funding for states to enhance their exisƟng registry to meet naƟonal standards.
* * *
Well-Integrated Screening and EvaluaƟon for Women Across the NaƟon (WISEWOMAN) Program The compe ƟƟve CDC WISEWOMAN cardiovascular disease reducƟon grant provides healthy lifestyle services for persons 35 to 64 who meet the eligibility for the CDC NaƟonal Breast and Cervical Cancer Early DetecƟon Program. The overall goal is to reduce hypertension and other chronic diseases through educaƟon, referrals for social needs, and healthy lifestyle programs and coaching focused on adopƟng healthier habits. In Pennsylvania, this program is known as the PA WISE Healthy Hearts, a cardiovascular disease (CVD) risk reducƟon program that provides healthy lifestyle programs and coaching. The goals are to help vulnerable par Ɵcipants understand and reduce their CVD risks, especially controlling and managing their hypertension; and reducing dispariƟes in CVD health, as heart disease remain the leading cause of death in Pennsylvania.
* * *
Environmental Public Health Tracking Program The objecƟve of this grant is to build public health capacity and experƟse in environmental health surveillance and data modernizaƟon to make informed decisions to improve public health. It supports the crea Ɵon and maintenance of a web-based system of health and environmental data. This includes funding for capacity building and infrastructure development. Recipients are expected to carry out the strategies and acƟviƟes to achieve short, intermediate, and long-term Page 23 of 307Page 23 of 307
* * *
outcomes under the areas of surveillance, data disseminaƟon/IT, outreach and communicaƟons, partnership enhancement, and program capacity development.
* * *
Environmental Health Capacity (EHC) Program The objec Ɵve of this program is to strengthen the capacity to protect public health by strengthening the environmental health (EH) pr ograms by providing technical resources and outreach support. This will ensure safe and healthy environments and improve community health status. The program encompasses three main strategies: (1) use EH data and informaƟon for data driven decision making; (2) idenƟfy and address EH hazards; and (3) assess the eﬀecƟveness and impact of EH services and interven Ɵons. Recipients are expected to carry out the program’s capacity-building strategies and ac ƟviƟes to achieve the goals outlined in the program’s logic model. The funding is used to expand PA’s exis Ɵng EH programs to become more robust and proacƟve. The program uses mulƟple sources of data on environmental risk factors and health to idenƟfy pressing EH issues and vulnerable popula Ɵons and develop educa Ɵon based EH intervenƟons across the Commonwealth. The focus areas include idenƟfying high-risk areas and reducing exposure to radon, contaminants in private drinking wells, and harmful algal blooms, with a concentra Ɵon on protec Ɵng families with young children. The Departments of Environmental Protec Ɵon and Conserva Ɵon and Natural Resources as well as Penn State Extension and Women for a Healthy Environment con Ɵnue to provide ongoing feedback on public-facing maps and other outreach eﬀorts.
* * *
Pennsylvania OccupaƟonal Safety and Health Surveillance (PennOSHS) Program PennOSHS is funded as part of the state occupaƟonal health surveillance program by the NaƟonal InsƟtute of OccupaƟonal Safety and Health, a CDC agency. This program aims to prevent and reduce occupa Ɵonally linked injuries, illnesses, deaths, and dispari Ɵes in Pennsylvania. OccupaƟonal health (OH) dispariƟes may lead to overall health inequiƟes that have the potenƟal to impact wellbeing of workers, their families, and their communiƟes. PennOSHS works to collect, compile, and analyze OH data to iden Ɵfy target areas and relevant ac Ɵons to be taken by employers and stakeholders to improve workplace safety. Addi Ɵonally, PennOSHS priori Ɵzes idenƟfying and reducing sources of lead exposure among adult Pennsylvanians through the Adult Blood Lead Epidemiology and Surveillance program component. Partnerships with the PA Department of Labor and Industry, Occupa Ɵonal Safety and Health Administra Ɵon, OH professionals, and other PA employers and organiza Ɵons help ensure the dissemina Ɵon of new OH ﬁndings and development of relevant educaƟonal materials.
* * *
Special Preparedness IniƟaƟves BioWatch is a U.S. Department of Homeland Se curity (DHS) program that operates as an early warning bio-detecƟon network. The program’s purpose is to detect pathogens, speciﬁcally agents of bioterrorism, that have been inten Ɵonally released into the air. Air samples are collected and rouƟ nely tested for the presence of deox yribonucleic acid (DNA) of select Page 24 of 307Page 24 of 307
* * *
organisms. A con ﬁrmed posiƟve laboratory test is ref erred to as a BioW atch Ac Ɵonable Result (BAR). The BioWatch system of air sampling and laboratory tesƟng can assist public health oﬃcials in determining the presence of a biological release in the environment. Early warning of a biological release enables local, state, and federal oﬃcials to assess risks to public health, iniƟate a criminal epidemiological inves ƟgaƟon, and implement emergency response ac ƟviƟes such as mass prophylaxis to mi Ɵgate the impact on the a ﬀected populaƟon. In Pennsylvania, DHS has idenƟﬁed Philadelphia and surrounding metrop olitan areas as a BioWatch jurisdic Ɵon. The Department of Health Bureau of Laboratories (BOL) serves as a host facility for the BioWatch program and provides laboratory space, scienƟﬁc experƟse, and IT support. BOL is a member of the Centers for Disease Control and PrevenƟon’s Biological Laboratory Response Network (LRN B) that conducts tesƟng to detect microorganisms potenƟally used in bioterrorism. BOL’s LRN-B laboratory performs addiƟonal tesƟng when BioWatch tesƟng yields a BAR. BOL receives limited funding from DHS to compensate it for some of the costs of supporƟng the BioWatch program in Pennsylvania.
* * *
State Loan Repayment Program This grant supports the Department’s ini ƟaƟve to provide funding for student loan repayment assistance to primary health care pracƟƟoners serving underserved areas of the Commonwealth. Eligible medical occupa Ɵons include physicians, den Ɵsts, psychologists, physician assistants, cerƟﬁed registered nurse pracƟƟoners, cerƟﬁed nurse midwives, registered dental hygienists, public health dental hygiene prac ƟƟoners, licensed clinical social workers, licensed counselors, and marriage and family therapists. In exchange for primary care service in approved areas for two years, parƟcipants receive student loan repayment assistance. Maximum awards are $80,000 for doctorate-level providers and $48,000 for other qualifying providers.
* * *
Public Health Emergency Preparedness & Response Funding is al located to showcase measurable and sustainable progress in advancing public health and healthcare preparedness ini ƟaƟves that enhance resilient and well-prepared communiƟes. The Bureau of Emergency Preparedness and Response (BEPR) oversees the aƩainment of the Public Health Preparedness Capabili Ɵes and Response Ready Framework as promulgated by the CDC. BEPR also works to achieve the NaƟonal Healthcare Preparedness and Response CapabiliƟes as deﬁned by the AdministraƟon for Strategic Preparedness and Response (ASPR). These naƟonal standards are geared towards enhancing and progressing not only BEPR’s readiness and response endeavors but also suppor Ɵng the public health and healthcare sectors across the Commonwealth. BEPR collaborates closely with local health departments, healthcare faciliƟes, other state agencies, and acts as the intermediary with Pennsylvania’s O ﬃce of Homeland Security and the Pennsylvania Emergency Management Agency (PEMA). Serving as the focal point within the Department of Health (DOH), BEPR assists in preparing for, safeguarding against, responding to, and recovering from all public health and healthcare impacts from emergencies aﬀecƟng the populaƟon. Page 25 of 307Page 25 of 307
* * *
Substance Use PrevenƟon, Treatment, and Recovery Services Block Grant (SUPTRSBG) Funding is used to provide staƟsƟcal data support to the Department of Drug and Alcohol Programs.
* * *
Learning Management System This appropriaƟon provides funding that supports the operaƟon and maintenance of the online Learning Management System (LMS), which provides training for the Pennsylvania Emergency Management Agency, the State Fire Academy Resident Program, Fire Fighter and Emergency Medical System (EMS) CerƟﬁcaƟons, the public health workforce, the health care workforce, and other local training opportuni Ɵes. The current LMS leverages training opportuniƟes from a wide range of state and naƟonal partner organizaƟons.
* * *
BioWatch Training BioWatch provides funding for overarching technical and management support for laboratories engaged in con Ɵnual monitoring for biological agents, as part of the Laboratory Response Network.

Quality Assurance
* * *
These appropria Ɵons support the Department’s Quality Assurance (QA) programs for Nursing Homes; Home Health Care Agencies; Hosp ice/s; Birth Centers; Pediatric Extended Care Centers; Intermediate Care Facili Ɵes (ICF); Hospitals; Ambulatory Surgical Facili Ɵes (ASFs); AborƟon FaciliƟes; Generic Equivalent Drugs; Drugs, Devices, and CosmeƟcs; Safety InspecƟons; Hearing Aid Sales; Indoor Tanning; and Temporary Health Care Service Agencies.
* * *
Acute and Ambulatory Care The Division of Acute and Ambulatory Care is the state licensing agent for hospitals, ASFs, and aborƟon faciliƟes as well as the federal cerƟﬁcaƟon agent under the Center for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) for general acute care; cri Ɵcal access hospitals; swing-bed, rehabilitaƟon, and specialty hospitals; ASFs; psychiatric units; rehabilita Ɵon units; and portable radiology (mobile X-ray) units throughout Pennsylvania. The Division is responsible for survey, inspecƟon, and cerƟﬁcaƟon related to new, renovated, and/or expanded faciliƟes, new services, and faciliƟes closure. In accordance with the Health Care FaciliƟes Act, the Division is responsible for promulgaƟng regulaƟons, surveying for compliance with regulaƟons, and licensing the State’s general and special hospitals and licensed and registered ASFs. To ensure compliance with regulaƟons, the Division surveys all ASFs on an annual basis. The ASF CondiƟons of ParƟcipaƟon (COP) concentrate on improving QA and infecƟon control in ASFs. ASFs are surveyed for compliance with both the state hospital regulaƟons and the CMS COP for Medicare cerƟﬁcaƟon every three years. Upon compleƟon of licensure inspecƟons, the survey teams issue facility-speciﬁc ﬁndings, including statements of de ﬁciency where appropriate. The licensed facility is required to develop and submit a plan of correc Ɵon for Division review and acceptance. AŌer compleƟon of the survey process, the survey team recommends the type of license to be issued: regular, limited, or provisional; and any penal Ɵes or sancƟons for failure to comply with licensure regulaƟons or Federal COP. Possible penalƟes and sancƟons include loss of license, closure of service, provisional license, civil penalƟes, ban on admission, CMS terminaƟon of deemed status for accredited facili Ɵes, and/ or loss of Medicare cer ƟﬁcaƟon. Unannounced follow-up inspecƟons assess the eﬀecƟveness of the facility in implemenƟng and monitoring the plan of correcƟon submiƩed in response to ﬁndings of noncompliance (statement of deﬁciency). All facili Ɵes submit plans of correc Ɵon using the online system. This supports rapid turnaround for the transmission of statements of de ﬁciency and facility responses, as well as public access to both the ﬁndings of the Department and the responses of faciliƟes in their plans of correc Ɵon. Survey ﬁndings and the facility plans of correc Ɵon are available to the public through the Department of Health website. In addiƟon to licensure and cer ƟﬁcaƟon surveys and follow-up, the Division inves Ɵgates complaints to ensure quality care is provided to pa Ɵents within the Commonwealth. Both state and federal complaint inves ƟgaƟons are unannounced. This func Ɵon is crucial to iden Ɵfy and correct deﬁcient pracƟces in the delivery of paƟent care. Page 31 of 307Page 31 of 307
* * *
Events occurring on hospital campuses or in ASFs, which may jeopardize the health and safety of individuals, must be reported to the Division in accordance with Title 28, Chapter 51 NoƟﬁcaƟon and Act 13 of 2002, the Mcare Act. Hospitals, ASFs, birthing centers, as well as psychiatric hospitals licensed by the Department of Human Services (DHS), are reported through the Pennsylvania Pa Ɵent Safety Repor Ɵng System (PA-PSRS). Professional sta ﬀ in the Division review serious event and infrastructure failure reports in PA-PSRS and determine if on-site invesƟgaƟon is necessary to protect paƟent health and safety. These are unannounced invesƟgaƟons. The informaƟon is transmiƩed from the PA-PSRS to the Department’s database. With the linkage of the PA-PSRS database and this system, redundant data entry is eliminated. In addi Ɵon, Federal Aspen Central Oﬃ ce databases and PA Automated Complaint Tracking System are used to support federal tracking and reporƟng related to Medicare cerƟﬁcaƟon and complaint invesƟgaƟon.
* * *
Nursing Care FaciliƟes The Division of Nursing Care Facili Ɵes (DNCF) is responsible for the licensing and cerƟﬁcaƟon of Pennsylvania's nursing faciliƟes. FaciliƟes are inspected for compliance with state licensure regulaƟons annually and at least once during a ﬁŌeen-month period for compliance with federal cer ƟﬁcaƟon standards, if par ƟcipaƟng in the Medicare or Medicaid programs. FaciliƟes that demonstrate a poor performance pa Ʃern or have serious compliance allega Ɵons against them are inspected more frequently. The Department receives par Ɵal funding from the federal government for conduc Ɵng inspecƟons of facili Ɵes parƟcipaƟng in the Medicare or Medicaid programs. Federal funding is also provided to nursing faciliƟes for services rendered to eligible residents when the Department determines, through on-site inspecƟon, that federal standards are met. Failure of the Department to comply with survey protocols mandated by the federal government may result in a ﬁnancial penalty to the Commonwealth. Failure on the part of a facility to meet program standards can result in a recommendaƟon to the DHS or the federal government to terminate facility funding. DNCF oversees the Department’s complaint hotline for all divisions that fall under the Oﬃce of QA. Complaints are received through a toll-free telephone line and/or online form. DNCF enters complaint informa Ɵon into the Department’s complaint database and no Ɵﬁes the appropriate division of the complaint. All nursing home complaints are invesƟgated promptly by professional survey staﬀ, either oﬀsite or through on-site unannounced complaint invesƟgaƟons. All complaints related to services not under the Oﬃce of QA are appropriately acknowledged and referred to by the respecƟve outside agencies. DNCF maintains the federally mandated Nurse Aide Registry through a contracted vendor. To maintain employment at a nursing care facility (NCF), an individual must be enrolled as a nurse aide in good standing on the registry within 4 months of employment. A link to the Nurse Aide Registry is available on the Department’s website and allows easy access to informa Ɵon related to the status of nurse aides. DNCF is responsible for reviewing all allegaƟons of abuse that occur in NCF s. Nurse Aide allega Ɵons are reviewed, and a commiƩ ee determines if further acƟ on, Page 32 of 307Page 32 of 307
* * *
leading to annotaƟon in the registry, is necessary to assure resident safety. FaciliƟes must verify that aides in their employment or those being considered for employment meet registry eligibility criteria and have no annotaƟons of substanƟated resident abuse, neglect, or misappropriaƟon of a resident’s personal property. The Department also ensures the safety and wellbeing of nursing home residents across the state, and that other state nurse aide registries are properly noƟﬁed of Pennsylvania’s registry acƟviƟes, by informing providers and out-of-state registries of annotated nurse aides in Pennsylvania.
* * *
Safety InspecƟon The Division of Safety InspecƟon provides Life Safety Code building analyses in accordance with federal and state mandates. This inspec Ɵon informa Ɵon is combined with the health inspecƟons by the DNCF, ICFs, Home Health, or Acute and Ambulatory Care to determine compliance with federal cerƟﬁcaƟon and state licensure health and safety requirements. FaciliƟes inspected include but are not limited to NCFs, ICFs for individuals with intellectual disabili Ɵes (ICF/IDs), hospitals, nonaccredited psychiatric ho spitals, hospices, ambulatory surgical centers, birthing centers, pediatric extended care faciliƟes, end stage renal disease faciliƟes, and aborƟon faciliƟes. Prior to construc Ɵon or renova Ɵon, the Division reviews all health care facili Ɵes’ plan drawings to ensure the proposed project conforms with state and federal requirements pertaining to ﬁre safety and funcƟonal environment for the safe and eﬃcient delivery of paƟent care. Plan reviews are conducted in person and through online submission. The Division performs Life Safety Code Occupancy Inspec Ɵons on all construc Ɵon, altera Ɵons, and renova Ɵons for health care faciliƟes. A health care facility is prohibited from occupying any newly constructed, altered, or renovated space for paƟent care prior to receiving occupancy approval from both the Division of Safety InspecƟon and the division responsible for the health inspecƟon. The Division prepares and evaluates Fire Safety EvaluaƟon Systems (FSES) for exisƟng health care faciliƟes that do not comply with the prescripƟve requirements of the current ediƟon of the Life Safety Code. The FSES is a complex measuring system used to assess equivalency between a building with a level of safeguards that diﬀer from those of the Life Safety Code, to the level of safety in a building that conforms exactly with the Life Safety Code.
* * *
Home Health The Division of Home Health (DHH) plays a criƟcal role in safeguarding the health and well being of Pennsylvanians by ensuring that a wide range of health care providers consistently deliver safe, eﬀecƟve, and high-quality care. The Division is responsible for overseeing providers through both licensure and cer ƟﬁcaƟon processes, aligning with state requirements as well as CMS standards. By doing so, DHH not only protects paƟents but also ensures providers remain eligible for federal reimbursement, which supports access to essenƟal health services across the Commonwealth. Page 33 of 307Page 33 of 307
* * *
DHH conducts on-site surveys and inspecƟons of Home Health Agencies, Hospices, Rural Health Clinics, End-Stage Renal Disease facili Ɵes, Comprehensive Outpa Ɵent Rehabilita Ɵon FaciliƟes, and OutpaƟent Physical Therapists. These evaluaƟons assess compliance with minimum operaƟonal standards, as well as the quality and safety of care delivered. For faciliƟes seeking to parƟcipate in federal programs, DHH recommends providers for Medicare cerƟﬁcaƟon, ensuring that vulnerable populaƟons can access covered services. Beyond cerƟﬁcaƟon, DHH also directly licenses a broader range of providers, including Home Health Agencies, Hospices, Birth Centers, Pediatric Extended Care Centers, Home Care Agencies, and Home Care Registries. Each of these providers addresses speci ﬁc needs within Pennsylvania’s health care system: for example, hospices deliver compassionate end-of-life care, pediatric extended care centers support medically fragile children, and home care agencies extend criƟcal assistance to individuals wishing to remain in their homes. To safeguard pa Ɵents and hold providers accountable, DHH operates a centralized complaint intake system, which includes both a statewide hotline and an online complaint form. Complaints received through this system are inves Ɵgated to ensure that consumers’ rights are protected and that de ﬁciencies are addressed promptly. This oversight process not only strengthens compliance but also empowers paƟents and families by giving them a clear avenue to report concerns.
* * *
Intermediate Care Facili Ɵes for Individuals with Intellectual Disabili Ɵes, Intermediate Care FaciliƟes/Other Related CondiƟons, and Psychiatric ResidenƟal Treatment FaciliƟes The Division of ICF is the regulatory agency responsible for ensuring the health, safety, and welfare of individuals with intellectual disabiliƟes or other related condiƟons living in faciliƟes in the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. The legal authority for the Division’s regulatory acƟviƟes is derived from Title XIX of the Social Security Act, Ar Ɵcles IX and X of the Public Welfare Code, and the Life Safety Code. The Division of ICF inspects facili Ɵes for compliance with federal cer ƟﬁcaƟon standards through unannounced surveys. Schedules are established annually to facilitate mee Ɵng the federal and state requirements. The survey team size for any facility is based on the facility populaƟon. Surveys are generally completed within two to ﬁve days, depending upon the size and complexity of the facility. The Division of ICF is also responsible for inspecƟng complaints, either oﬀ-site or through on-site unannounced complaint invesƟgaƟons.
* * *
Drugs, Devices, and CosmeƟcs This program ensures that manufacturers, distributors, and retailers comply with the statutory requirements of the Controlle d Substance, Drug, Device and CosmeƟ c Act, Noncontrolled Substances ReporƟng and RegistraƟon Act, and the Wholesale Drug Distribu Ɵon Licensing Act and regulaƟons as they relate to the manufacture, distribuƟon, and retail of drugs, controlled substances, list 1 chemicals, medical devices, and cosmeƟcs. The ﬁrms are registered with the Department and are inspected periodically or on an as-needed basis. Immediate on-site Page 34 of 307Page 34 of 307
* * *
inspecƟons are conducted when complaints or problems are indicated. The program also oversees the schedule of controlled substances and, when necessary, works with the Secretary of Health to schedule or reschedule substances through the regulatory process.
* * *
Hearing Aid RegistraƟon This program registers hearing aid ﬁƩers, apprenƟce ﬁƩers, temporary ﬁƩers, and dealers in Pennsylvania. Program staﬀ administer the Hearing Aid FiƩer ExaminaƟon for apprenƟces and review and resolve complaints from hearing aid purchasers. Applicants for ﬁƩer registraƟon will conƟnue to be registered and tested according to statewide mandates. RegistraƟons are renewed annually a Ōer fees are paid by ﬁƩers and dealers. Consumer complaints will con Ɵnue to be handled through follow-up by Department staﬀ on all complaints received and, if needed, on-site inspecƟons. Sta ﬀ occasionally work with the A Ʃorney General’s O ﬃce on complaints and violaƟons of the Hearing Aid Sales Law.
* * *
Tanning Bed RegistraƟon The Indoor Tanning RegulaƟon Act (Act 41 of 2014) created a comprehensive framework for the registraƟon and oversight of tanning facili Ɵes in Pennsylvania. Any loca Ɵon oﬀering UV tanning for compensa Ɵo n m u s t o b t a i n a D e p a r t m e n t o f H e a l t h r e g i s t r aƟon cer Ɵﬁcate before operaƟng, with annual renewal required. The Act de ﬁnes tanning facili Ɵes broadly to include salons, gyms, beauty o ﬃces, and similar establishments, and sets Ɵered registraƟon fees based on the number of tanning units. Facili Ɵes must post cer Ɵﬁcates prominently, maintain detailed customer records for at least three years, and comply with inspecƟ ons that may review operaƟons, records, training, and adherence to safety standards. The law also established strict requirements for operator training, safety signage, and protecƟve eyewear, while mandaƟng wriƩen warnings for customers. To protect minors, the Act prohibits use by anyone under 16 and requires pa rental consent for 17-year-olds. All fees and penalƟes support an Indoor Tanning RegulaƟon Fund, with the Department authorized to deny, suspend, or revoke registra Ɵons and enforce correcƟve ac Ɵons. These measures collec Ɵvely strengthen consumer safety, regulate industry pracƟces, and ensure consistent oversight across all tanning faciliƟes in the Commonwealth.
* * *
Temporary Health Care Services Agencies (THCSA) Ch. 8-B of the Health Care Facili Ɵes Act, enacted as Act 128 of 2022, mandates that any enƟty operaƟng as a temporary health care services agency—de ﬁned as organiza Ɵons placing temporary registered nurses, LPNs, nurse aides, or direct care sta ﬀ in long-term care nursing faciliƟes, personal care homes, or assisted living residences—must register annually with the Department and report all opera Ɵng loca Ɵons. The registra Ɵon applica Ɵon must include ownership informa Ɵon, corporate documents (if applicable), and a ƩestaƟons of readiness to make agency records accessible to the Department. Agencies must also demonstrate compliance with key operaƟonal standards: verifying staﬀ credenƟals and health quali ﬁcaƟons; maintaining Page 35 of 307Page 35 of 307
* * *
medical malprac Ɵce insurance, workers’ compensa Ɵon, and dishonesty bonds; adhering to employer withholding requirements; conduc Ɵng criminal background checks; and retaining records for 10 years. The Department is authorized to oversee temporary health care services agencies through complaint inves ƟgaƟons and enforcement ac Ɵons. Agencies must correct de ﬁciencies upon noƟce or submit correcƟve plans, and failure to comply may result in sancƟons including denial, suspension, or revocaƟon of registraƟon, or civil penalƟes of up to $5,000 per incident—each day of noncompliance counted separately. Addi Ɵonally, the Act includes a mandatory Ɵmeline: agencies operaƟng at enactment had 180 days to register, whereas new agencies must register within 90 days of launch.
* * *
Health Care Associated InfecƟons The Healthcare Associated InfecƟon PrevenƟon (HAIP) Sec Ɵon supports hospitals, NCFs, and ASFs by: reviewing and approving individual facility infec Ɵon control plans; providing direct consultaƟon to facility infec Ɵon prevenƟonists; collaboraƟng with the Bureau of Epidemiology, the PaƟent Safety Authority, and the Pennsylvania Health Care Cost Containment Council; sharing best prac Ɵces for monitoring, surveillance, and respon se to HAI; developing and issuing data validaƟon reports; conduc Ɵng on-site visits and outreach phone calls to determine compliance and provide assistance with Act 52 requirements; and establishing benchmarks for hospitals and nursing homes to prevent, reduce, and eventually eliminate healthcare associated infecƟons.
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons Medicare The purpose of the Medicare reimbursement program is to ensure that hospitals, home health agencies, nursing homes, hospices, ambulatory surgical centers, rural health centers and other Medicare-eligible providers of health serv ices meet the minimum health care standards mandated by federal rules and regula Ɵons. These faciliƟes are inspected to determine if health care standards are being met and to cer Ɵfy to the federal government that the level of quality exists, thus making providers eligible for Medica re funding. This program also includes funding for Nursing Care Facili Ɵes Minimum Data Sets, Home Health Outcome and Assessment InformaƟon Set, and the Nursing Home Oversight and Improvement Program.
* * *
Medicaid CerƟﬁcaƟon The purpose of the Medicaid reimbursement program is to ensure that nursing homes, intermediate care facili Ɵes for individuals with intellectual disabili Ɵes, psychiatric residen Ɵal treatment faciliƟes, and other Medicaid-eligible facili Ɵes meet minimum health care standards mandated by federal rules and regula Ɵons. These facili Ɵes are inspected to determine if the health care standards are being met and to cer Ɵfy to the federal government that the level of quality exists, thus making the provider eligible for Medicaid funding. ## Health PromoƟon and Disease PrevenƟon
This appropria Ɵon extends support to improve maternal health in Pennsylvania, parƟcularly in popula Ɵons where inequi Ɵes are iden Ɵﬁed. Funds are used to provide infrastructure and programming to reduce maternal morbidity and mortality across the Commonwealth with a focus on Black individuals, individuals living in rural areas, and individuals with behavioral health challenges including substance use disorder. Ini ƟaƟves funded through this appropriaƟon include: • Regional Maternal Health Coali Ɵons: Coali Ɵons were formed in four areas of Pennsylvania and are responsible for implemen Ɵng recommenda Ɵons from the Pennsylvania Maternal Mortality Review Commi Ʃee (MMRC) to improve maternal health. • The Philadelphia Organized Voice for Ac Ɵon (OVA): Serving as the acƟon arm of the Philadelphia MMRC, the OVA works across sectors to develop innova Ɵve strategies, allocate experƟse and funding to pilot projects, and integrate community perspecƟves and soluƟons into policies and programs to improve pregnancy-associated outcomes in Philadelphia. • Perinatal TiPS: Consulta Ɵon services to prenatal, labor and delivery, postpartum, family, and community-based healthcare pr oviders for mental health and substance use-related needs. • Healthy Start Behavioral Health Ini ƟaƟve: Expanding mental and behavioral health services at all six Healthy Start sites in PA. • Doula services, including expanding the doula workforce: Trainings to become a doula, speciﬁcally for people of color, and doula services to individuals living in Lancaster, Dauphin, and York coun Ɵes, with priority given to popula Ɵons dispropor Ɵonally aﬀected by maternal mortality and morbidity. • Promising Maternal Health IniƟaƟves: ImplemenƟng innov aƟve strategies to address needs of the pregnant and postpartum populaƟons and improve health. ## Achieving BeƩer Care – MAP AdministraƟon
Act 191 of 2014 established the Achieving Be Ʃer Care by Monitoring all Prescrip Ɵons Program (ABC-MAP) and the ABC-MAP Board. The ABC-MAP program is responsible for implemenƟng an enhanced prescripƟon drug monitoring program (PDMP) system and processes for prescribers to refer paƟents to substance use disorder treatment and implemenƟng the ABC MAP Board’s policies and proc edures related to educaƟon, outreach, idenƟﬁcaƟon and referral of at-risk individuals to substance use disorder treatment, compiling sta ƟsƟcs, research, and educaƟonal materials and outreach. The ABC-MAP program is governed by a Board of state agency department heads. The Board is responsible for appoinƟng an advisory group comprised of dispensers, prescribers, law enforcement oﬃcials, addicƟon specialists, pa Ɵent and privacy advocates, and individuals with experƟse in the opera Ɵon of the PDMP system. The Department is required to administer the program by performing administraƟve and support services as directed by the board.
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons PrescripƟon Drug Monitoring The Overdose Data to Ac Ɵon in States (OD2A-S) provides funding to State Health Departments (SHDs) to enhance their ability to track and prevent nonfatal and fatal overdoses while also idenƟfying emerging drug threats. The funding emphasizes surveillance strategies and the promoƟon of evidence-based and evidence-informed intervenƟons that have an immediate impact on reducing overdose morbidity and mortality, with a focus on opioids, s Ɵmulants, and polysubstance use. OD2A-S is underpinned by a data-to-acƟon framework that reinforces the use of surveillance and other data to inform and drive preven Ɵon e ﬀorts and policies, with an emphasis on addressing health equity and health dispari Ɵes. This funding builds o ﬀ work and gains from previous overdose surveillance and prevenƟon investments supporƟng SHDs. The Harold Rogers PDMP provides funding to support a variety of PDMP implementaƟon or enhancemen t acƟviƟes that encourage the use of PDMPs to improve clinical decision-making and prevent the abuse and diversion of controlled substances. The First Responders-Comprehensive Addic Ɵon and Recovery Program establishes processes, protocols, and mechanisms for referral to appropriate treatment and recovery communiƟes, and safety around fentanyl, carfentanil, and other dangerous licit and illicit drugs. This program also allows ﬁrst responders and members of other key community sectors to administer a drug or device approved under the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosme Ɵc Act for emergency treatment of known or suspected opioid overdose. The Strategic PrevenƟon Framework for PrescripƟon Drugs grant program is designed to raise awareness about the dangers of sharing medica Ɵons and work with pharmaceu Ɵcal and medical communiƟes on the risks of overprescribing to young adults. The program also raises community awareness and brings prescripƟon drug abuse prevenƟon acƟviƟes and educaƟon to schools, communiƟes, parents, prescribers, and their paƟents. ($ Amounts in Thousands) Vital Statistics State $ Federal $ Other $ Total PERSONNEL 1. Chan ge in Budgetary Reserve: $0 ($38) $0 ($38) Subtotal Budgetary Reserve $0 ($38) $0 ($38) TOTAL $0 $415 $0 $415 Page 55 of 307Page 55 of 307
* * *
Vital StaƟsƟcs
* * *
This appropria Ɵon funds the statewide vital sta ƟsƟcal program, which includes registering, preserving, and maintaining the integrity of all birth, death, and fetal death records ﬁled in the Commonwealth in conjuncƟon with the Vital StaƟsƟcs Law of 1953 (P.L. 304, No. 66).
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons
* * *
CooperaƟve Health StaƟsƟcs The Bureau of Health Sta ƟsƟcs and Registries is the o ﬃcial State Center for Health StaƟsƟcs. The State Center receives ongoing federal contract funds to support the Vital StaƟsƟcs CooperaƟve Program, the NaƟonal Death Index, the Social Security EnumeraƟon at Birth Project, and the Social Security Death Match/Fraud PrevenƟon Project. Speciﬁc programs include:
* * *
Vital StaƟsƟcs CooperaƟve Program This program is funded by the NaƟonal Center for Health StaƟsƟcs and Centers for Disease Control and PrevenƟon (CDC) and is a coaliƟon of data providers and users at federal, state, and local levels of government. The goals are to collect, compile, and disseminate vital staƟsƟcs data in the most e ﬃcient and economical system possible. The con Ɵnuing goal of this program is to eliminate duplicaƟon in data collecƟon, and to implement standard procedures at the state level of data collec Ɵon, thereby providing comparable data with other states and ensuring that the vital staƟsƟcs database for Pennsylvania meets federal requirements.
* * *
The NaƟonal Death Index (NDI) This program is funded by the Na Ɵonal Center for Health StaƟsƟcs and is an informaƟon system that is used to determine the cause of death for individuals included in medical and health-related research. The principal advantage of the NDI is that deaths for all states are consolidated into a single ﬁle, so a death for a given individual can be located regardless of where the death occurred.
* * *
EnumeraƟon at Birth Project This project is funded by the Social Security Administra Ɵon (SSA) and allows the SSA in cooperaƟon with the Department to provide, on a voluntary basis, the service of assigning a Social Security number to a newborn based on informa Ɵon obtained as part of the state birth registraƟon process. Parents can beneﬁt from using this voluntary program by not having to visit a Social Security oﬃce in person.
* * *
Page 56 of 307Page 56 of 307
* * *
## Social Security Death Match/Fraud PrevenƟon Project
The SSA also provides funding for receipt of selected Department death ﬁles. These ﬁles are matched with SSA beneﬁciary ﬁles. This match of records reduces fraud and abuse by ensuring that SSA does not make bene ﬁt payments to deceased persons. Based on this match and conﬁrming informaƟon, SSA can prevent overpayment to those persons for whom SSA either has no record or has recorded a date of death which diﬀers substanƟally from the date in Department ﬁles. Death CerƟﬁcaƟon Project This project is funded by the U.S. Consumer Product Safety Commission and provides the Commission with Ɵmely informaƟon of deaths caused by or related to consumer products. Health StaƟsƟcs This program receives funding from the U.S. Department of Labor for the Census of Fatal OccupaƟonal Injury Program, which provides for a comprehensive, veriﬁable, and accurate count of fatal occupaƟonal injuries. This program is part of a naƟonal eﬀort to develop and maintain an ongoing occupaƟonal fatality database from which work-related injury prevenƟon strategies can be developed. The program requires that occupaƟonal fataliƟes be substanƟated by at least two independent source documents. The Department gathers informaƟon from several sources and veriﬁes work-related fataliƟes occurring in Pennsylvania. These sources include death cerƟﬁcates, Workers’ CompensaƟon reports, fatal motor vehi cle accident reports, Occupa Ɵonal Safety and Health AdministraƟon reports, and newspaper ar Ɵcles. SubstanƟated cases are processed and submiƩed to the U.S. Department of Labor. Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System These funds, in combina Ɵon with funding from the CDC, pay for a statewide probability survey using landline telephones and cellphones which measures state progress toward meeƟng Healthy People objecƟves in areas such as physical acƟvity and ﬁtness, nutriƟon, tobacco, asthma, unintenƟonal injuries, oral health, heart disease and stroke, cancer, diabetes, etc. for Pennsylvania adults. Data on the prevalence of chronic disease and health risks are essen Ɵal for determining high-risk populaƟons for health promoƟon and disease prevenƟon programs and for evaluaƟng the impact of statewide policies. ## Vital StaƟsƟcs Improvement AdministraƟon
This appropriaƟon funds the statewide vital sta ƟsƟcs program, including all sta ﬃng and administraƟve expenses associated with the Vital Sta ƟsƟcs Improvement Account, and for costs of various vital sta ƟsƟcs systems improvement projects as s Ɵpulated by Act 122 of 2004. The statewide vital records program includes registering, preserving, and maintaining the integrity of all birth, death, and fetal death records ﬁled in the Commonwealth in conjuncƟon with the Vital StaƟsƟcs Law of 1953 (P.L. 304, No. 66). The Bureau of Health StaƟsƟcs and Registries represents a core func Ɵon of government in protec Ɵng these important legal and historical documents; ensuring the physical security and conﬁdenƟality of these records; and issuing cerƟﬁed copies of birth and death cerƟﬁcates to eligible applicants via mail, in-person, and online services. Vital Records branch oﬃces provide in-person services for birth and death cerƟﬁcates to all eligible applicants. Local registrars provide in-person services speciﬁcally for funeral directors obtaining death cerƟﬁcates within 90 days of the registra Ɵon of the report of death, or 90 days aŌer a pending death is ﬁnalized by the coroner or medical examiner. Birth and death cerƟﬁcates are used for establishing iden Ɵty and ci Ɵzenship; obtaining driver’s permits and passports; providing proof of age for Social Security an d other government programs; and for estate proceedings. The vital sta ƟsƟcs program also provides a database for sta ƟsƟc al analysis, and enables public health research including cause of death, birth defects, and prenatal care among other key public health informa Ɵon. Disclosure of vital sta ƟsƟcs data for public health research purposes is governed by the Vital StaƟsƟcs Law of 1953. The Department began electronic repor Ɵng of births in 1997 and requires all licensed birthing and healthcare faciliƟes to report births electronically. In 2017, the Department began to migrate the reporƟng of deaths from a paper-based system to an electronic system. By December 2020, this electronic death registraƟon system (EDRS) was used by coroners/medical examiners, funeral homes, and local registrars, with 29% of deaths being fully reported and 64% of deaths being par Ɵally reported directly into EDRS. The Department con Ɵnues to work with medical cerƟﬁers to adopt EDRS. As a result of these e ﬀorts, electronic reporƟng was used in more than half of cases reported by medical facili Ɵes in 2023. The EDRS syst em was updated in October 2024, and post-transiƟon, about half of all death reporƟng remains fully electronic. Preliminary 2024 data: Of the 115,083 deaths re ported for the year, 53.2% of all deaths (61,227 cases) were fully electronically reported and 46.52% (53, 541 cases) were par Ɵally electronically reported. • 99.73% electronic death reporƟng by funeral homes (114,768 out of 115,083 total cases) • 95.46% electronic death reporƟng by coroner/ME oﬃces (19,604 out of 20,536 total cases) • 43.71% electronic death reporƟng by medical faciliƟes (41,089 out of 93,996 total cases) o 69.33% of hospital reporƟng (21,036 out of 30,341 cases) o 40.89% of nursing home reporƟng (10,094 out of 24,688 cases) o 45.69% of hospice reporƟng (1,526 out of 3,340 cases) Page 66 of 307Page 66 of 307
* * *
The beneﬁts of electronic reporƟng include improved (near-real-Ɵme) reporƟng of deaths to the Department, self-prin Ɵng of disposi Ɵon permits and in-system ordering of death cerƟﬁcates for funeral directors, streamlined reporƟng of amendments to reports of death, and more Ɵmely release of death data to government agencies and medical researchers for deaths that occur in Pennsylvania. Next, the Department intends to implement electronic repor Ɵng for fetal deaths. Fetal death reporƟng shares stakeholders with birth repor Ɵng (such as birthing hospitals) and death reporƟng (such as funeral homes, coroners, and medical examiners). AdopƟon of electronic death reporƟng has made signi ﬁcant strides, with nearly all funeral directors and coroner/ME o ﬃces using EDRS, and birthing hospitals are already required to report births electronically. Therefore, it is an Ɵcipated that it will be a rela Ɵvely simple, and desirable, transi Ɵon for these same stakeholders to begin using electronic methods instead of paper repor Ɵng for fetal deaths. The new fetal death system is planned to become available to Department sta ﬀ in late 2025 and onboarding of external stakeholders will begin in early 2026. Page 67 of 307Page 67 of 307
* * *

State Laboratory
* * *
The State Public Health Laboratory performs clinical laboratory analyses to iden Ɵfy infecƟous and noninfec Ɵous diseases throughout the Commonwealth, provides diagnos Ɵc support to physicians, conducts reference anal yses for other laboratories, and provides epidemiologic and surveillance support. The Bureau of Laboratories (BOL) regulates clinical laboratories both within and outside of Pennsylvania through the implementa Ɵon of both the Commonwealth’s Clinical Laboratory Act (35 Pa C.S. §2151-2165) and the federal Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988. BOL’s tesƟng funcƟons and oversight of clinical laboratories serving the Commonwealth ensure th e availability of quality clinical laboratory services for clinicians and other health care pr oviders for the proper diagnosis, treatment, and prevenƟon of disease. BOL performs specialized highly complex laboratory tes Ɵng. This includes cri Ɵcal tesƟng for rabies, inﬂuenza, measles, rubella, Lyme, chlamydia, tuberculosis, enteric diseases, botulism, meningiƟs, SARS-CoV-2, and arboviruses including but not limited to West Nile virus and Zika virus. BOL also provides outbreak inves ƟgaƟon support. In addi Ɵon, BOL conducts analyses of alcohol and controlled substances on specimens from persons who die in motor vehicle accidents. Specimens are submiƩed by county coroners and medical examiners. Results from this tesƟng are used to assess mortality related to driving while under the in ﬂuence of either alcohol or other drugs and to provide evidence for the death invesƟgaƟons or related legal proceedings. The State Public Health Laboratory is a member of the Centers for Disease Control and Preven Ɵon’s (CDC) Laboratory Response Network and has been designated by the CDC, the Federal Bureau of InvesƟgaƟon, and the US Postal Service as the Commonwealth’s reference laboratory for bioterrorism and chemical terrorism tesƟng. BOL conducts proﬁciency tesƟng and approval programs for laboratories that administer certain toxicologic analysis services in accordance with the regula Ɵons of the Commonwealth’s Clinical Laboratory Act. Currently, approvals are issued to conduct analyses for abused drugs in urine, alcohol in blood and serum, lead in bl ood, erythrocyte protoporphyrin in blood, and controlled substances in blood and serum. Lists of approved laboratories are published semi annually as noƟces in the Pennsylvania BulleƟn. Laboratories pay fees to enroll in these programs.
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons
* * *
Clinical Labor atory Improvement The Department regulates approximately 10,000 clinical laboratories within and outside of Pennsylvania through the implementaƟon of the Commonwealth’s Clinical Laboratory Act (35 Pa C.S. §§2151-2165) and the federal Clinical Laboratory Improvement Amendments of 1988. On site inspecƟons, proﬁciency tesƟng assessments, and personnel training are u Ɵlized to ensure that laboratories generate accurate and reliable results. Page 72 of 307Page 72 of 307
* * *
## Epidemiology & Laboratory Surveillance and Response
The purpose of the Epidemiology a nd Laboratory Capacity for Infec Ɵous Diseases (ELC) CooperaƟve Agreement with the CDC is to build on the state’s eﬀorts to strengthen our capacity to recognize and respond to emerging (and re-emerging) infecƟous disease threats by enhancing our basic epidemiologic, laboratory, and health informa Ɵon system capacity. The ELC program focuses on no Ɵﬁable diseases, food-, water-, and vector-borne diseases, vaccine preventable diseases, and drug-resistant infecƟons. It is intended to support acƟviƟes that enhance the ability of a program to: iden Ɵfy and monitor the occurrence of infec Ɵous diseases of public health importance in a community; characterize disease determinants; idenƟfy and respond to disease outbreaks and other infec Ɵous disease emergencies; use public health data for priority se ƫng and policy development; and assess the e ﬀecƟveness of ac ƟviƟes. Strengthening collaboraƟon between health informa Ɵon systems, laboratory, and epidemiology prac Ɵce is a crucial component of this program. The NaƟonal AnƟmicrobial Resistance Monitoring System for Enteric Bacteria (NARMS) is a collaboraƟon among state and local public health departments, the CDC, the U.S. Food and Drug AdministraƟon (FDA), and the U.S. Department of Agriculture (USDA). This naƟonal public health surveillance system tracks changes in the anƟmicrobial suscepƟbility of certain enteric (intesƟnal) bacteria found in ill people (CDC), retail meats (FDA), and food animals (USDA) in the United States. The NARMS program helps protect public health by providing informaƟon about emerging bacterial resistance, the ways in which resistance is spread, and how resistant infec Ɵons diﬀer from suscepƟble infecƟons.

## State Health Care Centers
The Bureau of Community Health Systems operates a network of 59 state health centers across six districts that act as the implementa Ɵon arm for the Department’s public health programs. The state health centers operate under the administraƟve and programmaƟc direcƟon of the Division of State Health Centers, whose sta ﬀ provide coordina Ɵon, consulta Ɵve and administraƟve support to these centers. Services include communicable disease clinical services, family health programs, and environmental health services. In addiƟon, the state health centers engage in community health assessment and educaƟonal outreach programs to promote healthy behaviors. Community Health Nurses also invesƟgate reportable diseases and prevent/manage communicable disease outbreaks. The Bureau administers the annual registra Ɵon of over 600 organized camps, and the Public Bathing Place Program, which regulates and inspects over 4,600 public bathing place faciliƟes. Responsibili Ɵes include inves ƟgaƟng complaints, processing applica Ɵons, conduc Ɵng inspecƟons, issuing permits, and performing regulatory enforcement acƟviƟes for public bathing place faciliƟes and coordinaƟng with other state agencies in ma Ʃers related to organized camp sanitaƟon and regulaƟon. The Bureau provides educaƟon and guidance on Environmental Health related concerns to ciƟzens throughout the Commonwealth and is responsible for educaƟon and cerƟﬁcaƟon of Local Health Oﬃcers that serve the municipaliƟes throughout the Commonwealth.
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons Disease Control ImmunizaƟon The US Department of Health and Human Services has designated vaccinaƟon among one of the top ten greatest public health achievements of the 20th century. The Bureau of ImmunizaƟons pr ovides statewide leadership in the ongoing e ﬀort to protect Pennsylvania’s children, adolescents, and adults from vaccine-preventable diseases and to ensure the safety of vaccines. The Bureau focuses on several major programma Ɵc areas, including child, adolescent, and adult immuniza Ɵons; vaccine-preventable disease surveillance and outbreak control; immunizaƟon coverage assessments and immuniza Ɵon informa Ɵon system development, maintenance, and support; public provider an d Vaccines for Children (VFC) private provider vaccine distribu Ɵon; vaccine and provider quality assurance reviews; professional and public educaƟon; school and childcare facility immuniza Ɵon coverage reports; outreach awareness acƟons and emergency preparedness and response partnership eﬀorts. Vaccines of focus for infants and children include: measles, mumps, rubella, polio, diphtheria, tetanus, pertussis, Hemophilus inﬂuenza type b, hepaƟƟs B, varicella, pneumococcal rotavirus, in ﬂuenza, COVID, and respiratory syncy Ɵal virus (RSV); for adolescents: measles, mumps, rubella, diphtheria, tetanus, hepa ƟƟs A and B, human papillomavirus, meningococcal disease, varicella, inﬂuenza, and COVID; and for adults: inﬂuenza, tetanus, diphtheria, pertussis, hepaƟƟs A and B, shingles, pneumococcal disease, RSV, and COVID. The Bureau’s goal for an Page 78 of 307Page 78 of 307
* * *
immunizaƟon coverage rate for all recommended vaccines generally coincides with the Healthy People 2030 goals. The Bureau will ensure that providers, parents, and the public have access to vaccines for the provision of immuniza Ɵons; ensure that adolescents have access to the recommended vaccines; and enhance the adult in ﬂuenza and pneumococcal vaccine outreach with speciﬁc emphasis toward adult populaƟons in low vaccine coverage areas. Vaccines are rouƟ nely distributed to department state health centers and other department-enrolled providers, county and mu nicipal health departments, Federally Quali ﬁed Health Centers (FQHCs)/Rural Health Centers (RHCs), and more than 1,300 private and public health care providers enrolled in the VFC Progra m. During the most recent year, approximately 1.7 million doses of vaccines were distributed (e xclusive of Philadelphia, which is its own immunizaƟon jurisdic Ɵon and CDC awardee) to public and private provider sites. The VFC Program has a distribu Ɵon system to make vaccines available to any public and private health care provider at no cost to be administered to persons 0-18 years of age who are Medicaid enrolled, have no health insurance, or are American Indian/Alaskan NaƟve; and to underinsured eligible persons in FQHCs/RHCs. The Bureau has iden Ɵﬁed geographic areas across the Commonwealth at risk for under immunizaƟon. Resources and strategies will be con Ɵnued in these areas to promote the importance of immunizaƟon. The statewide Perinatal HepaƟƟs B PrevenƟon Program facilitates the follow-up with vaccinaƟons and prophylaxis for those infants born to and contacts of chronic hepaƟƟs B posiƟve females. The Bureau works with the O ﬃce of Child Development and Early Learning to survey state-licensed childcare facili Ɵes to assess immunizaƟon records for children at the faciliƟes. These assessments are used to target low immuniza Ɵon coverage areas for educaƟon and follow-up. The assessments show low coverage by anƟgen and by county.

PHHSBG – Block Program Services Asthma Control Program Program goals are to reduce asthma hospitalizaƟons and hospital emergency room visits, while increasing primary care visits and controller (versus rescue) medica Ɵons; increase the number of people with asthma receiving home environmental assessment and self-management educaƟon and eliminate asthma-related health dispariƟes and reduce asthma burden.
* * *
Diabetes PrevenƟon and Control The Diabetes PrevenƟon and Control Program focuses on three major goals: to improve the lives of Pennsylvanians with diabetes, to prev ent the risk for type 2 diabetes among adults with prediabetes, and to improve self-care prac Ɵces, quality of care, and early detec Ɵon of complicaƟons among people with diabetes. Program outcomes are tracked through the Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System and data from the Pennsylvania Health Care Cost Containment Council, other surveillance-type data sources, contractor reports, and feedback from stakeholders.

## Heart Disease and Stroke Program
The purpose of the Heart Disease and Stroke Program is to reduce premature morbidity and mortality from heart disease and stro ke through primary and secondary preven Ɵon and control e ﬀorts. Heart disease and stroke are the leading and third leading causes of death, respecƟvely, among men and women in Pennsylvania. Primary preven Ɵon seeks to control high blood pressure, high blood cholesterol, type 2 diabetes, and obesity to prevent a ﬁrst event (heart aƩack or stroke). Secondary prevenƟon seeks to reduce the risk of recurrent events. Services to address primary and secondary prevenƟon and their modiﬁable risk factors are delivered through agreements with statewide professional organizaƟons and community partners.
* * *
Child, Adolescent, and Adult Obesity The Obesity Preven Ɵon and Wellness Sec Ɵon implements evidence-informed strategies to address food and nutriƟon security; increase access to nutriƟous foods and beverages in health system seƫngs; implement high-impact obesity prevenƟon standards in early care and educaƟon systems; provide training and technical assistance to school districts on Comprehensive School Physical AcƟvity Program and the Whole School, Whole Community, Whole Child Model; and provide supports to communi Ɵes to implement community planning and transporta Ɵon intervenƟons to support safe and accessible physical acƟvity and acƟve transportaƟon.
* * *
Oral Health Program The Oral Health Program collaborates with other governmental agencies, local community groups, school nurses, dental hygienists, and local denƟsts and their associaƟons on oral health promoƟon eﬀorts. Other program aspects include collaboraƟon with agencies on access to dental health services for the underserved, evidence-based educa Ɵon, and awareness programs; and serving as liaison to the dental profession.
* * *
Violence and Injury PrevenƟon Program The Violence and Injury Preven Ɵon Program is dedicated to reducing the incidence of injuries and violence across communiƟes in Pennsylvania. Its purpose is carried out by developing strong surveillance systems, implemenƟng evidence-based prevenƟon strategies and educaƟon programs tailored to popula Ɵons at greatest risk. Through these e ﬀorts, the program seeks to address both uninten Ɵonal injuries and acts of violence, promote safer environments, and ulƟmately improve the overall health and well-being of individuals and families across the state.
* * *
Sexual Violence PrevenƟon and EducaƟon Program The Sexual Violence Preven Ɵon and Educa Ɵon Program provides funding to Respect Together to support 48 rape cris is centers through a federal statutory set-aside for services to rape vicƟms and prevenƟon.
