## PrevenƟve Health Special Projects
The Oral Health Program collaborates with other governmental agencies, local community groups, school nurses, dental hygienists, and local denƟsts and their associaƟons on oral health promoƟon eﬀorts. Other program aspects include collaboraƟon with agencies on access to dental health services for the underserved, evidence-based educa Ɵon and awareness programs; and serving as liaison to the dental profession. The purpose of the NaƟonal Violent Death ReporƟng System is to collect and disseminate accurate, Ɵmely, and comprehensive surveillance data on all violent deaths using the CDC guidelines and a web-based data entr y system. With this system, the e ﬀecƟveness of violence prevenƟon iniƟaƟves will be increased by increasing the ability to design, target, implement, and evaluate prevenƟon programs. The Asthma Control Program supports the goals and objec Ɵves of the Healthy People 2030 focus area for respiratory diseases and is working to reduce the burden of asthma through eﬀecƟve management and control. The goals of the program are to improve asthma control and management and the quality of life for people with asthma to reduce the number of deaths, hospitalizaƟons, emergency department visits, school days or workdays missed, and limita Ɵons on ac Ɵvity due to asthma. Two main strategies are being used to accomplish these goals: 1) Improving organizaƟonal infrastructure to advance greater health equity and sustainability by implemenƟng a strategic plan in collabora Ɵon with partners; advancing health equity partnerships with community organiza Ɵons, mul Ɵ-sector organiza Ɵons, and community members to achieve meaningful community engagement in program decision-making; strengthening asthma surveillance and repor Ɵng to drive strategic ac Ɵon and program improvement; and using evaluaƟ on and performance measurement for con Ɵnuous quality improvement, to replicate successful interven Ɵons, and to support health equity and sustainability eﬀorts. 2) Expanding the implementa Ɵon of an evidence-based mul Ɵ-component technical package across mul Ɵple sect ors for popula Ɵons with a high asthma burden. This includes expanding access and delivery of asthma self-management educaƟon; making referrals to smoking cessa Ɵon programs to eliminate smoking a nd exposure to second-hand smoke; expanding access and delivery of home visits fo r asthma triggers, environmental assessments, and asthma self-management educa Ɵon; using quality improvement ini ƟaƟves to achieve guidelines-based medical management of asthma; promoƟng coordinated care and linkages with community resources; and promoƟng environmental policies and best pracƟces to reduce indoor and outdoor asthma triggers.
* * *
CollaboraƟve Chronic Disease Programs The Division of Tobacco Preven Ɵon and Control (DTPC) receives federal funds from the CDC and the Food and Drug Administra Ɵon (FDA) to develop, implement, and support strategic and culturally appropriate e ﬀorts to reduce tobacco product use and exposure to secondhand smoke in Pennsylvania to enhance the quality of life for all residents.
* * *
Page 81 of 307Page 81 of 307
* * *
The DTPC u Ɵlizes CDC funding to: 1) prevent the ini ƟaƟon of tobacco use (including emerging products and e-cigareƩes) among youth and young adults, 2) promote quiƫng among adults and young people, 3) eliminate nonsmo kers’ exposure to secondhand smoke, and 4) idenƟfy and eliminate tobacco-related health dispariƟes. DTPC meets these goals by collaboraƟng with public health programs and agencies to increase preven Ɵon educaƟon and access to quit services in Pennsylvania, u Ɵlizing community-led approaches to address popula Ɵons that are disparately aﬀected by tobacco use. The DTPC implements statewide intervenƟons and acƟviƟes to address the epidemic of emerging tobacco product use, including e-cigare Ʃes, among youth, and focus on educa Ɵng stakeholders, youth inﬂ uencers and community partners to prevent iniƟaƟon and reduce use and access to emerging tobacco products. With these funds, the DTPC engages partners, sustains coali Ɵons, and educates stakeholders about health and the beneﬁ ts of proven tobacco regula Ɵons and policies. The DTPC also coordinates enforcement eﬀ orts to monitor every PA tobacco retailer for tobacco sales compliance and uƟlizes earned media eﬀorts to educate and promote services. The DTPC conducts program evaluaƟon and facilitates the use of data to inform all public health acƟons. The DTPC u Ɵlizes FDA funding to enforce provisio ns of the federal Family Smoking PrevenƟon and Tobacco Control Act (Tobacco Control Act). The FDA has authority to regulate the manufacturing, markeƟng, and distribuƟon of tobacco products to protect the public health and to reduce tobacco use by minors as well as regulate certain health warnings that must appear on smokeless tobacco products. The DTPC conducts FDA tobacco enforcement inspecƟons at retail establishments in Pennsylvania that sell and adverƟse regulated tobacco products to determine compliance with the provisions and submit inspecƟon results to FDA. The DTPC collects tobacco related evidence of completed FDA tobacco enforcement inspec Ɵons and supports the FDA in any enforcement or judicial ac Ɵons, including c oordinaƟng the dra Ōing and execu Ɵon of declaraƟons by the Commissioned Oﬃ cers and narraƟve reports by the Commissioned O ﬃcers and Underage Purchasers who par Ɵcipated in FDA tobacco enforcement inspec Ɵons, arranging for their tesƟmony if necessary, and furnishing tobacco and tobacco-related evidence.

Sexual Violence PrevenƟon and EducaƟon This grant builds upon eﬀorts to address sexual violence prevenƟon using a public health approach, as well as support strategies and ac ƟviƟes that prevent sexual violence from ini Ɵally occurring and reduce ﬁrst Ɵme perpetra Ɵon and vic ƟmizaƟon of sexual violence through comprehensive primary prevenƟon programming and evaluaƟon.

Live Healthy Diabetes PrevenƟon and Control Program The Diabetes PrevenƟon and Control Program focuses on three major goals: to improve the lives of Pennsylvanians with diabetes, to prev ent the risk for type 2 diabetes among adults with prediabetes, and to improve self-care prac Ɵces, quality of care, and early detec Ɵon of complicaƟons among people with diabetes. NaƟonal Cardiovascular Health Program Through the Na Ɵonal Cardiovascular Health Program, the Department implements and evaluates a comprehensive, evidence-based, a nd evidence-informed cardiovascular disease (CVD) preven Ɵon and management program to improv e cardiovascular health and reduce inequiƟes and health care dispariƟes in high-risk priority populaƟons across the Commonwealth. The Program strives to improve blood pressure control and reduce blood pressure dispari Ɵes among targeted popula Ɵons within partner healthcare and community se ƫngs and increase uƟlizaƟon of and mi Ɵgate social support barriers among priority popula Ɵons at highest risk of CVD, with a focus on hypertension and high cholesterol. This is accomplished through increased use of Electronic Health Records or Health InformaƟon Technology to report, monitor, and track detecƟon of health care dispari Ɵes, support communica Ɵon and coordina Ɵon among mulƟdisciplinary care team members, and idenƟfy, manage, and treat paƟents at the highest risk of CVD with emphasis on hypertension and cholesterol management. The Department addresses idenƟﬁed barriers to social services and support needs within populaƟons at highest risk of CVD with the assistance of the CVD learning collabora Ɵve as well as promote increased use of mulƟdisciplinary teams and adherence to evidence-based guidelines. The Department also works to increase the engagement of Community Health Workers to provide care beyond standard clinical intervenƟons and increase community-clinical links to iden Ɵfy, respond to, and address social services and support needs of populaƟons at highest risk of CVD.
* * *
Paul Coverdell NaƟonal Acute Stroke Program In 2001, Congress provided funding to CDC to establish the Paul Coverdell NaƟonal Acute Stroke Registry. The program has since expanded and became the Paul Coverdell NaƟonal Acute Stroke Program. The aim has been to support the implementa Ɵon of comprehensive stroke prevenƟon and management strategies across the con Ɵnuum of care, from the onset of stroke symptoms through rehabilitaƟon and recovery. The program has conƟnued to expand by focusing on evidence-based heart disease and stroke prevenƟon acƟviƟes for high-risk populaƟons, which include those who have experienced a stroke and those with uncontrolled or undiagnosed hypertension.

## The Whole School, Whole Community, Whole Child (WSCC)
Through the WSCC grant, the Department collaborates with partners to convene a statewide school health coali Ɵon, facilitate statewide professional development and technical assistance in a variety of WSCC related areas and implement the WSCC framework with Erie City School District (ECSD). In collabora Ɵon with the Pennsylvania Department of Educa Ɵon, the Department will build upon an exis Ɵng health and physical educa Ɵon stakeholder group to develop a coali Ɵon with statewide representa Ɵon from all WSCC areas. The coaliƟ on guides professional development, technical assistance, and resources to be o ﬀered statewide through exisƟng events with intermediate units and Society for Health and Physical Educators. Training is oﬀered statewide and open to all 500 school districts, but ﬁnancial assistance, technical assistance, and resources will be targeted to districts located in areas experiencing high poverty and disproporƟonately aﬀected by chronic diseases and aƩributable risk factors. The Department provides training and technical assistance, along with funding to support a district wellness coordinator to improve healthy eaƟng, physical acƟvity, and chronic disease management among students in ECSD.
* * *
Refugee Health Program This subgrant from the PA Department of Human Services (DHS) provides funding for staﬃng to coordinate and oversee refugee medical and mental health screenings and iden Ɵfy emerging health condiƟons; processing migrants to other states and providing technical support; provide training and health educaƟon and disseminaƟng educaƟonal materials; conducƟng onsite monitoring and comprehensive repor Ɵng; coordinaƟng and collabora Ɵng with key partners to improve and expand refugee health services; evalua Ɵon of annual sta ƟsƟcal results to provide recommendaƟons to improve health screenings and referrals; and coordina Ɵon to ensure seamless funcƟoning of the Refugee Health Program when surges in numbers require addiƟonal support. Prior to May 1, 2016, the enƟre Refugee Health Program (RHP) and funding resided in the Bureau of Epidemiology (BOE). In May 2016, BOE retained the State Refugee Health Coordinator, and the rest of the program sta ﬀ went to the DHS along with the funding. Since May 1, 2016, Coor dinator and contracted RHP Associate Epidemiologist Specialist are funded by the subgrant. The O ﬃce of Refugee Rese Ʃlement provides federal grants to DHS to manage refugee reseƩlement and refugee health programs. Page 84 of 307Page 84 of 307

## Sexually TransmiƩed Disease Screening and Treatment
The goal of the Sexually TransmiƩed Disease (STD) Program is to reduce the incidence of syphilis, gonorrhea, and chlamydia. The STD Program supports comprehensive STD preven Ɵon, disease interven Ɵon, and treatment services throughout the Commonwealth (exclusive of Philadelphia). STD clinical services are provided in over 100 locaƟons across the Commonwealth. These locaƟons include state health centers, contracted health care providers via Par ƟcipaƟng Provider Agreements, and county and muni cipal health departments (CMHDs). Using a contracted laboratory, the Department provides syphilis, gonorrhea, chlamydia, and HIV tes Ɵng through contracted STD clinics and state health centers. AnƟbioƟcs are supplied to clinical service sites by the STD Program for the treatment of pa Ɵents and their sex partners. Funding for STD prevenƟon and treatment acƟviƟes is provided through a combinaƟon of state and federal funds. In addiƟon, CMHDs receive funds under the Local Health AdministraƟon Law (Act 315) to include STD prevenƟon and treatment services. The City/County of Philadelphia is designated as a separate STD project area from the rest of the Commonwealth based on federal funds received from the Centers for Disease Control and PrevenƟon. Communica Ɵon is vital and well-established between the two project areas, as Philadelphia’s disease burden comprises a large por Ɵon of the overall reported morbidity from the State. Disease interven Ɵon personnel (including community health nurses and disease intervenƟon specialists) are posi Ɵoned throughout the state and in CMHDs to conduct HIV and STD inves ƟgaƟons including partner services, linkage to tes Ɵng, risk-reduc Ɵon counseling, treatment, and care. To create awareness, staﬀ conduct provider and paƟent outreach educaƟon throughout the state. Individuals are interviewed to conﬁrm treatment and refer sex partners for care and treatment. The STD Program has established a minimum standard for ﬁeld invesƟgaƟons: • Pa Ɵen ts diagnosed posiƟve for primary or secondary syphilis, • Pregnant individuals with syphilis, chlamydia, and/or gonorrhea (for follow-up to prevent complicaƟons among newborns, including congenital syphilis), • Teens 15 and under who test posi Ɵve for chlamydia and/or gonorrhea, • Individuals co-infected with an STD and HIV, • Individuals with repeat gonorrhea infecƟons.
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons
* * *
Survey & Follow-up STD This appropria Ɵon focuses on tes Ɵng, treatment, counseling, partner no ƟﬁcaƟon, and risk-reducƟon eﬀorts for three major reportable STDs: chlamydia, gonorrhea, and syphilis.

## Diabetes Control Program
The Diabetes PrevenƟon and Control Program focuses on three major goals: to improve the lives of Pennsylvanians with diabetes, to decrease the risk for type 2 diabetes among adults with prediabetes, and to improve self-care prac Ɵces, quality of care, and early detec Ɵon of complicaƟons among people with diabetes.
* * *
Program outcomes are tracked through the Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System and data from the Pennsylvania Health Care Cost Containment Council, other surveillance-type data sources, contractor reports, and feedback from stakeholders. Page 99 of 307Page 99 of 307

## Primary Health Care PracƟƟoner
The Primary Health Care PracƟƟoner program was established by Act 113 of 1992. Chapter 13 of the Act, Primary Care to Medically Underserved Areas, empowers the Department to create iniƟaƟves designed to enhance the availability of primary health care pracƟƟoners in the Commonwealth. This includes a focus on increasing the number of primary health care pracƟƟoners in underserved rural and urban areas within the state.
* * *
Primary Care Loan Repayment Program (LRP) The Department allocates funding to facilitate student loan repayment assistance for primary health care pracƟƟoners delivering services in underserved areas of the Commonwealth. Eligible medical occupaƟons include physicians, denƟsts, psychologists, physician assistants, cerƟﬁed registered nurse pracƟƟoners, cerƟﬁed nurse midwives, registered dental hygienists, public health dental hygiene pracƟƟoners, licensed clinical social workers, licensed counselors, and marriage and family therapists. In return for providing primary care service in designated areas, parƟcipants received student loan repayment assistance for a duraƟon of two years.
* * *
Waiver Programs A J-1 visa is issued to internaƟonal medical graduates who wish to complete medical educaƟon in the United States and requires them to return to their home country for two years before applying for permanent residency in the United States. Under the Conrad State 30 J-1 Visa Waiver Program, the federal ImmigraƟon and NaƟonality Act permits state departments of health to request a waiver of up to 30 J-1 physicians each year in exchange for a three-year commitment of the physicians to provide services to residents of medically underserved communiƟes at pracƟce sites approved by the Department. Under the federal Appalachian Regional Commission (ARC), the Department may recommend addiƟonal J-1 waivers for primary care physicians who will provide care in underserved communiƟes in the 52 counƟes of Pennsylvania which are included in the ARC. ARC J-1 waivers require a three-year commitment with no limit on the number of waivers that may be supported by ARC in Pennsylvania. Furthermore, a NaƟonal Interest Waiver allows primary care physicians to gain quicker access to permanent residency status provided the physician agrees to complete an addiƟonal two-year commitment in an underserved area aŌer compleƟon of the three-year J-1 Visa Waiver commitment. This program is beneﬁcial to the underserved residents in Pennsylvania because it either provides conƟnuing services to residents if the physician was in Pennsylvania during the J-1 Visa Waiver commitment or it provides addiƟonal access if the physician is moving into Pennsylvania from another state.
* * *
Page 104 of 307Page 104 of 307
* * *
## Area Health EducaƟon Center (AHEC)
The Department provides funding in support of primary health care workforce development for rural and underserved areas in Pennsylvania to the Pennsylvania State University (PSU) College of Medicine, AHEC Program. Through seven regional oﬃces, the PSU College of Medicine AHEC program coordinates clinical training rotaƟons for medical and dental students and for primary care medical and dental residents at community-based clinical training sites located in underserved areas of the commonwealth. In addiƟon to funding received from the Department, the PSU College of Medicine receives funding from the federal Health Resources and Services AdministraƟon AHEC program to develop a comprehensive system which: 1) provides community-based training opportuniƟes for health professions students; 2) provides conƟnuing educaƟon programs for health professionals; and 3) supports the recruitment of primary health care providers from underserved areas and minority communiƟes.
* * *
Oﬃce of Rural Health The Department allocates funds to the PSU Oﬃce of Rural Health (ORH) to assist the Pennsylvania Primary Care Oﬃce (PCO) in fulﬁlling its legislaƟve mandate to enhance the supply and distribuƟon of primary care pracƟƟoners in underserved rural counƟes of Pennsylvania. In addiƟon to funding received from the Department and PSU, the ORH receives funding from the federal Oﬃce of Rural Health Policy. The funds provided under the Department’s contract are used by the ORH to support the objecƟves of its federal grant. The federal grant requires the ORH to fulﬁl three core funcƟons and one or more opƟonal funcƟons. The three required funcƟons are: 1) to serve as an informaƟon clearinghouse; 2) to provide technical assistance; and 3) to coordinate resources and acƟviƟes statewide. In addiƟon to the required funcƟons, the ORH performs two further funcƟons for the PCO: support of recruitment and retenƟon eﬀorts and strengthening of state and federal partnerships. These ﬁve funcƟons provide the framework for developing and implemenƟng the contract’s three-year work plan in support of the Department’s goals. The work plan also supports the goals and objecƟves of the State Health Improvement Plan iniƟated by the Department. This ensures the most eﬀecƟve and eﬃcient use of resources in support of rural health in Pennsylvania.
* * *
> “Bridging the Gaps” Community Health Internship Program
The Department allocates funding to the University of Pennsylvania for the Bridging the Gaps Community Health Internship Program. This seven-week summer iniƟaƟve oﬀers students in the health and social service professions a collaboraƟve, interdisciplinary, community-based educaƟon experience. ParƟcipants engage in community-based projects that address pressing public health issues, including maternal and child health, HIV/AIDS, and prevenƟve health. Emphasis is placed on health promoƟon and client educaƟon among medically underserved populaƟons. The program is in operaƟon in Philadelphia, PiƩsburgh, Erie, and the Lehigh Valley.
* * *
Page 105 of 307Page 105 of 307
* * *
PA AssociaƟon of Community Health Centers (PACHC): PA Primary Care Career Center Program The Department allocates funds to PACHC to support the Pennsylvania Primary Care Career Center which assists community-based health care centers located in, or serving, underserved areas of the commonwealth to recruit and retain primary care pracƟƟoners. The program acƟvely promotes Pennsylvania employment opportuniƟes to medical residents and other health professions students throughout the commonwealth and naƟonally. It also provides recruitment services that match suitable candidates for employment with vacancies at health centers which are adverƟsed and promoted by the center.
* * *
Pennsylvania Academy of Family Physicians (PAFP): Primary Care Residency Expansion Program The Department allocates funding to PAFP to support the expansion of residency opportuniƟes for medical school graduates seeking to complete residency in family medicine in Pennsylvania. This program provides funds to exisƟng family medicine residency programs which train residents for future service in rural and underserved communiƟes to expand their programs by adding addiƟonal residency slots. Priority for matching medical graduates to these slots is given to Pennsylvania ciƟzens and graduates of Pennsylvania’s medical schools. Medical residents recruited into these new slots provide primary care services during their residency training in rural and underserved areas. The medical residents are also provided with professional development opportuniƟes throughout their training which includes career planning with a focus on future pracƟce in Pennsylvania.
* * *

## _35 P.S. § 10227.101-102; 10227.111-1113; 10227.5101_
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
This appropriation provides grants to community-based health care clinics located in underserved areas or serving low-income populations. Grants are provided to develop new community-based health clinics; expand primary health care services at existing clinics; add or expand prenatal, obstetric, postpartum and newborn care at existing clinics; develop alternative health care delivery systems at existing clinics to reduce hospital emergency room usage; and implement collaborative relationships between community-based clinics, hospitals and other health care providers. Disbursements are based on grant agreements with eligible applicants. Page 109 of 307Page 109 of 307
* * *
## Community-Based Health Care Subsidy
The Community-Based Health Care Program wa s established by Act 10 of 2013. This legislaƟon empowers the Department to provide gran ts to community-based health care clinics located in underserved areas or serving low-income popula Ɵons. The objecƟves of the program are to: develop new clinics; expand primary health care services at exisƟng clinics; add or expand prenatal, obstetric, postpartum, and newborn care at exis Ɵng clinics; develop alternate health care delivery systems at exisƟng clinics to reduce hospital emergency room usage; and implement collaboraƟve relaƟonships between community-based health clinics, hospitals, and other health care providers.
* * *
Eligible applicants for these gr ant funds include Federally Quali ﬁed Health Centers (FQHCs) and FQHC Look-Alikes, CerƟﬁed Rural Health Clinics (non-proﬁt), Hospital Health Clinics (non-proﬁt), Free or ParƟal Pay Clinics, and Nurse Managed Care Clinics (non-proﬁt). Page 110 of 307Page 110 of 307

## _35 P.S. § 621 et seq., Act 36 of 2008_
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
This appropriation supports the Newborn Screening and Follow-up Program (NSFP). Funding provides screening for approximately 145,000 births. The NSFP also administers a metabolic formula program for phenylketonuria (PKU) clients through age 21 and beyond for females pursuing pregnancy. Services are provided via agreements with seven newborn screening treatment centers and one contracted laboratory. Page 113 of 307Page 113 of 307
* * *
Newborn Screening
* * *
This appropriaƟon supports the Newborn Screening and Follow-up Program established by the Newborn Child TesƟng Act of September 9, 1965 (P.L. 497, No. 251) and amended by Act 36 and Act 133. All newborns in Pennsylvania ar e mandatorily screened for 37 dried blood spot condiƟons, hearing loss, and cri Ɵcal congenital heart disease. The Act also indicates that condiƟons added to the Recommended Uniform Screening Panel will be added to the Pennsylvania panel with approval of the advisory board and condiƟons can be nominated to the advisory board for addi Ɵon. Since 2022, four condi Ɵons have been added to the Pennsylvania screening panel. The program also provides follow-up services for criƟcal congenital heart defect screenings as provided under th e Newborn Child Pulse Oximetry Screening Act, and hearing screenings as provided under the Infant Hearing EducaƟon, Assessment, ReporƟng, and Referral Act.

## Cancer Screening Services
The Pennsylvania Breast and Cervical Cancer Early DetecƟon Program (PA-BCCEDP) is a breast and cervical cancer screening program th at provides free breast and cervical cancer screenings to women who are Pennsylvania residents. Women qualify for PA-BCCEDP to receive free breast and cervical cancer screening and diagnosƟc services, including mammograms, clinical breast exams, pelvic exams, and Pap tests if they are 40 to 64 years old (or under 40 if they are symptomaƟc); they have no insurance, or limited insurance that does not cover breast and cervical cancer screening services or cannot pay the co-payment or deducƟble, and they have low to moderate income (under 250% of the Federal Poverty Income Guidelines). The PA-BCCEDP is also funded through the Federal Na Ɵonal Breast and Cervical Cancer Early DetecƟon Program (NBCCEDP) which was established by the Centers for Disease Control and PrevenƟon (CDC) a Ōer the passage of the Breast and Cervical Cancer Mortality Preven Ɵon Act of 1990 (Public Law 101-354).

## _35 P.S. § 521.1 et seq.; 35 P.S. § 7601 et seq.; 71 P.S. § 532, 532(a); 42 U.S.C. 300ff-11 et seq., 12901 et seq., 247c(b-c),_

Disbursement Criteria: AIDS Programs and Special Pharmaceutical Services funding is used to develop and implement a multi-dimensional, coordinated strategy to prevent and change high-risk behaviors, and provide resources and direction for avoiding infection with the HIV virus. The Special Pharmaceutical Benefits Program (SPBP) provides funding for HIV/AIDS drugs and drugs used to treat life threatening AIDS-related illnesses and lab services for individuals living with a diagnosis of HIV/AIDS who are not eligible for pharmaceutical coverage under the Medical Assistance (MA) program. Income eligibility is set at 500 percent of the Federal Poverty Level. Services are provided through agreements with county and municipal health departments, as well as regional grantees. Drugs are provided via an agreement with Department of Aging. Page 121 of 307Page 121 of 307

## AIDS Program and Special PharmaceuƟcal Services
This appropriaƟon funds in part a state-wide comprehensive HIV program for the Department that includes the following High Impact PrevenƟon (HIP) Strategies and AcƟviƟes: • TesƟng services are provided through a statewide network of healthcare and non healthcare HIV tesƟng sites. MulƟple strategies, as well as the integraƟon of sexually transmiƩed disease and hepaƟƟs C tesƟng, are implemented depending upon the venue, to reach persons with undiagnosed HIV infecƟon and co-infecƟon. • Comprehensive prevenƟon for persons living with HIV (PLWH) consisƟng of linkage to HIV care, treatment, and prevenƟon services for those persons newly diagnosed with HIV or currently living with HIV; promoƟng retenƟon or re-engagement in care for those living with HIV; oﬀering referral and linkage to other medical and social services; and the provision of ongoing partner services (PS). • Evidence-based HIV prevenƟon intervenƟons, including status neutral intervenƟons which reach those at increased risk of acquiring HIV or those living with HIV. • Screening for Pre-exposure prophylaxis (PrEP) eligibility, referral, and linkage to PrEP for individuals at high risk for HIV infecƟon. Promote awareness and provide educaƟon regarding PrEP for clients and providers. Support access to PrEP for eligible uninsured and underinsured individuals. • CollecƟon and interpretaƟon of HIV data to characterize trends in HIV infecƟon, monitor clusters and detect potenƟal outbreaks, implement public health intervenƟons, and evaluate public health responses.
* * *
Funding parƟally supports HIV prevenƟon services through grants with seven county and four municipal health departments and a statewide network of fee-for-service providers through ParƟcipaƟng Pr ovider Agreements. This appropria Ɵon also parƟally funds regional HIV grantees, inclusive of the Philadelphia Department of Public Health, to complement the federal Ryan White Comprehensive AIDS Resource Emergency Act of 1990, as amended, for a comprehensive conƟnuum of medical and support services needed for PLWH and their families. Emphasis for the use of these funds by the regional grantees is placed on acƟviƟes in support of non-Ryan White eligible services which may include HIV prevenƟon for PLWH, including linkage to and retenƟon in care, and re-engagement for those who have fallen out of care. An Integrated HIV PrevenƟon and Care Plan assists with decision-making related to the use of state funds directed toward prevenƟon, care, and treatment services. This appropriaƟon in total is used to assist in meeƟng the Commonwealth’s state match requirement for the Ryan White CARE Act Title II grant funding. It also ensures the HIV Program’s ability to implement criƟcal HIV prevenƟon and care strategies and acƟviƟes that fall outside of the allowable scope of services under the federal appropriaƟons and grants such as some PrEP-related acƟviƟes, the integraƟon of viral hepaƟƟs and STD prevenƟon strategies where appropriate, and the services for PLWH who are co-infected or at risk for co-infecƟon with viral hepaƟƟs or other STDs. Page 123 of 307Page 123 of 307
* * *
Federal AppropriaƟons AIDS – Ryan White & HIV Care This program provides formula-based ﬁnancial assistance to states, and certain high incidence ciƟes, for the AIDS Drug Assistance Program/Special PharmaceuƟcal Beneﬁts Program for people living with HIV (PLWH) who meet certain eligibility criteria and are not eligible for pharmaceuƟcals under Medical Assistance programs. This appropriaƟon funds laboratory services, HIV anƟretroviral medicaƟons, drugs used to treat life-threatening opportunisƟc infecƟons, and other medicaƟons to support the overall health of enrolled PLWH. This is accomplished through health insurance premium assistance for enrolled clients or full payment. Matching funds of one dollar of state funds for every two dollars of federal funds is provided through AIDS Programs and Special PharmaceuƟcal Services. This program provides formula based ﬁnancial assistance to states, and certain high-incidence ciƟes, to improve the quality, availability, and organizaƟon of health care and support services for PLWH and their families. This is accomplished through funding the regional HIV grantees. Grantees enter into agreements for a comprehensive conƟnuum of medical and support services for PLWH and their families. These funds are used as payors of last resort; therefore, HIV rebate funds acquired through the 340b program are used ﬁrst to support the provision of these HIV care support services. The grantees and their sub-grantees are responsible for reporƟng informaƟon regarding client demographics and services provided. This informaƟon is used at agency, regional, and statewide levels for planning and reporƟng purposes. The data collected are elements idenƟﬁed by the Health Resource and Services AdministraƟon.
* * *
Housing for Persons with AIDS (HOPWA) The purpose of this program is to provide housing and associated supporƟve services to eligible low-income PLWH and their families. The Department is the designated recipient of HOPWA funds from the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD). The Department has designated regional grantees as the local administrators (except for the Philadelphia and PiƩsburgh eligible metropolitan staƟsƟcal areas, which receive direct HUD funding). The regional grantees fund community-based providers to deliver services. The City of Allentown, the City of Harrisburg, and Bensalem Township are also designated eligible metropolitan staƟsƟcal areas which may receive direct HUD funding; however, Allentown and Harrisburg have declined the program funding based on the administraƟve burden associated with implemenƟng the program. The Department has accepted the responsibility as a direct gr antee from HUD for these areas to administer this program. Eligible acƟviƟes funded under the grant include tenant-based rental assistance; short-term rent, mortgage, and uƟlity payments; permanent housing placement; supporƟve services; and operaƟng costs for housing.
* * *
AIDS Health EducaƟon Program This fund provides AIDS health educaƟon and other services to increase public awareness of AIDS-related issues and prevenƟon measures. Page 124 of 307Page 124 of 307
* * *

## _35 P.S. § 5631 et seq._
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
This appropriation provides funding for research and treatment to Pennsylvania cancer centers that provide cancer programs, which include, but are not limited to, direct care services, development of cancer trial programs, and development of education and community outreach programs. Page 127 of 307Page 127 of 307
* * *
## Regional Cancer InsƟtutes
This appropriation provides funding for educ ation, patient navigation, and addressing barriers to care to four Pennsylvania cancer centers: University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute, the University of Pennsylvania Cancer Center, Pennsy lvania State University Cancer Center, and the Northeast Regional Cancer Institute. Using the Pennsylvania State Cancer Control Plan, the cancer institutes provide evidence based interventions to reduce cancer disparities and increase equitable access to cancer care. Upon notification of available funds, these institutes submit a work statement for cancer projects appropriate for the level of funding available. Page 128 of 307Page 128 of 307

## _24 P.S. § 14-1401 et seq.; 24 P.S. § 25-2505; Act 55 of 2024_
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
The School Health Program is responsible for the healthy growth and development of all children of school age. It helps to eliminate health risks which, if left unchecked, would adversely affect quality of life and the ability to learn. Over two million children attending public, private and parochial schools benefit from comprehensive school services. The Public School Code of 1949 requires nine specific health services, including medical and dental health examination, vision and hearing screening tests, height and weight measurements, tuberculosis tests, threshold screening tests and special examinations. Disbursements are made based on a pre-established fee multiplied by the Average Daily Membership, or actual certified costs, whichever is less. Act 55 of 2024 directs the Department of Health, in consultation with the Department of Education, to use up to $3,000,000 to award grants for feminine hygiene products to school entities to be provided to students at no expense. Page 131 of 307Page 131 of 307
* * *

## School District Health Services
The School Health Program facilitates the healthy growth and development of children of school age. This program prevents and detects health problems and fosters the development of coordinated school health programs that strengthen the educaƟonal process by maintaining and improving the health status of children and by promo Ɵng healthy educa Ɵonal prac Ɵces and environments. ArƟcle 14 of the Pennsylvania Public School Code (Code) provides that all children aƩending public, private, and parochial schools re ceive school health services. These services include medical and dental examina Ɵons; ﬁve di ﬀerent health screenings; nursing services, including treatment of acute and chronic condi Ɵons, ﬁrst aid, and emergency care; medica Ɵon administraƟon; health counseling and health promo Ɵon; wellness educa Ɵon; maintenance of student health records; and compliance with immunizaƟon requirements. ArƟcle 25 of the Code provides for state reimbursement to districts for a por Ɵon of the costs associated with the provision of these school health services. The Division prescribes the content of the School Health Program; monitors district compliance with laws, regulaƟons, and policies; sets forth the duƟes of school health professional staﬀ; approves requests for modiﬁcaƟons to the mandated programs; provides consultaƟon and technical assistance to school districts to support and improve health services; fosters state and local cooperaƟon and coordinaƟon of services, and develops and implements special projects and iniƟaƟves for be Ʃerment of school health. The Department works with the Department of EducaƟon on developing rules, regula Ɵons, and standards for the e ﬃcient opera Ɵon and evaluaƟon of the School Health Program. The Division ensures health services are provid ed to students in 500 school districts, 10 full-Ɵme vocaƟonal technical schools, and over 175 charter schools. In addi Ɵon, the Division of School Health monitors schools’ complia nce with mandated services and provides reimbursement to public schools for health servic es. The School Health Program, part of the Bureau of Community Health Systems, con Ɵnues to signi ﬁcantly increase the collabora Ɵon between and integra Ɵon of programs and services of the Department’s district o ﬃces, county and municipal health departments, communiƟes, and local school districts. ## _16 P.S. § 12001 et seq._
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
This program supports public health initiatives approved by the Department after meeting criteria as set forwarded by Act 315 of 1951 and regulations. The following jurisdictions are served: Allegheny, Bucks, Chester, Delaware, Erie, Montgomery, and Philadelphia Counties; and the Cities of Allentown, Bethlehem, Wilkes-Barre, and York. Disbursements are based on a per capita formula. Local health departments receive $6.00 per capita or 50% of their actual expenditures, whichever is less. Grant recipients may use funds received only for services related to public health, either mandated by the Act or approved by the Department. Page 136 of 307Page 136 of 307
* * *
## VI. EXPLANATION OF CHANGES APPROPRIATION:
($ Amounts in Thousands) Local Health Departments State $ Federal $ Other $ Total GRANT & SUBSIDY 1. To maintain fundin g requirements per Local Health Administration Law: $411 $0 $0 $411 Subtotal Grant & Subsidy $411 $0 $0 $411 TOTAL $411 $0 $0 $411 Page 137 of 307Page 137 of 307
* * *
## Local Health Departments
This program supports public health ini ƟaƟves undertaken by county/municipal health departments. The jurisdic Ɵons currently served are Allegheny, Bucks, Chester, Delaware, Erie, Montgomery, and Philadelphia CounƟes, along with the CiƟes of Allentown, Bethlehem, Wilkes Barre, and York. The program requires that services be provided within the jurisdicƟonal boundaries of the approved health department in areas of communicable disease control. This includes tuberculosis and sexually transmiƩed disease control; public health laboratory services for the iden ƟﬁcaƟon of disease and its vectors; public health educa Ɵon for the improvement of health status; the analysis of health trends; maternal and child health services; chronic disease control; and public health nursing services to allow for intervenƟon with at-risk groups of the populaƟon served, to reduce and/or eliminate public health problems. Funding for this appropria Ɵon is provided through a formula contained in Act 315. The law allows for maximum funding at 50% of their budget, not to exceed $6.00 per capita. AddiƟonal funding is provided by categorical grants from the state and federal governments and through local funds, which may include revenue-genera Ɵng programs such as inspec Ɵon or licensing fees. Use of the fund by the departments is limited to this grant program. Grant recipients may use funds received only for services related to public health, and either mandated by the Act or approved by the Department. There is no local match required for eligibility. ## _16 P.S. § 12001, 12025(d) et seq._
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
This is a program established by Act 315 of 1951, as amended by Act 12 of 1976, to allow for funding of local health departments to provide environmental health services, as defined by the Act and Title 28, Part II, Chapter 17,
* * *
> "Standards for Environmental Health Services." The following jurisdictions participate in this program: Allegheny,
Bucks, Delaware, Chester, Erie, Montgomery, and Philadelphia Counties; and the Cities of Allentown, Bethlehem, Wilkes-Barre, and York. Page 141 of 307Page 141 of 307
* * *
## Local Health – Environmental
This program supports environmental health ini ƟaƟves undertaken by county/municipal health departments. The program requires acƟviƟes in food and water supply protecƟon, water polluƟon control, public bathing place sanita Ɵon, vector control, solid waste management, and inspecƟon of ins ƟtuƟonal, recrea Ɵonal, and housing environments. County/municipal health departments may oﬀer programs beyond those listed in any environmental area relevant to the needs of their jurisdic Ɵon. Target popula Ɵons are those of the county/municipal health departments' jurisdicƟons, including Allegheny, Bucks, Chester, Delaware, Erie, Montgomery, and Philadelphia CounƟes, along with the ciƟes of Allentown, Bethlehem, Wilkes-Barre, and York. Funding for this appropriaƟon is provided through a formula contained within the Act and is not to exceed $1.50 per capita. Addi Ɵonal funding is provided by categorical grants from the state and federal governments and through local funds, which may include revenue-genera Ɵng programs such as inspec Ɵon or licensing fees. Use of the fund by the departments is limited to this grant program. Grant recipients may use funds received only for services related to public health, and either mandated by the Act or approved by the Department. There is no local match required for eligibility. ## Maternal and Child Health
Funding is for the state share of the cost of screening Medical Assistance (MA) eligible newborns/children in the state-mandated Newborn Screening and Follow-Up Program (NSFP). This appropriaƟon supports the NSFP established by the Newborn Child Tes Ɵng Act of September 9, 1965 (P.L. 497, No. 251) and amended by Act 36 and Act 133. All newborns born in Pennsylvania are currently mandatorily screened for 37 dried blood spot condiƟons, hearing loss, and cri Ɵcal congenital heart disease. The Act also indicates that condi Ɵons added to the Recommended Uniform Screening Panel (RUSP) w ill be added to the Pennsylvania panel with approval from the advisory board. Since 2022, four condiƟons have been added to the screening panel via the state nominaƟon process or the RUSP. The NSFP also administers a Metabolic Formula program for phenylketonuria (PKU) clients through age 21 and beyond for females pursuing pregnancy.

Federal AppropriaƟons
* * *
Women, Infants, and Children (WIC) This appropriaƟon covers the costs of providing food beneﬁts to WIC parƟcipants.

Maternal and Child Health Services Block Grant (MCHSBG) – Program Services The current programming for the MCHSBG is a result of the 2025 Needs and Capacity Assessment. Through this assessment, seven priority needs were iden Ɵﬁed for the PA MCH populaƟon and a state acƟon plan with clearly deﬁned objecƟves and evidenced-based strategies has been created. The following are the seven prioriƟes and will be in eﬀect through September 30, 2030: 1. Behavioral Health During Pregnancy and Postpartum 2. High Quality and Respecƞul Maternal Healthcare 3. OpƟmal Health and Wellbeing for Infants 4. Preterm Birth and Preterm-Related Mortality 5. Early Childhood Development and OpƟmal Health 6. Adolescent Mental Health and Suicide PrevenƟon 7. Provider Access, Care CoordinaƟon, and NavigaƟon for Children and Youth with Special Health Care Needs
* * *
Teenage Pregnancy PrevenƟon Teenage pregnancy prevenƟon funds are provided to support the replicaƟon of evidence based program models that have been proven through rigorous evalua Ɵon to be e ﬀecƟve to reduce teenage pregnancy, behavioral risk factors underlying teenage pregnancy, or other associated risk factors. Page 147 of 307Page 147 of 307

AbsƟnence EducaƟon Funds will be used to implement sexual risk avoidance educaƟon that teaches youth, ages 10-19, to voluntarily refrain from sexual acƟvity.

Family Health Special Projects Pregnancy Risk Assessment Monitoring System (PRAMS) Grant The purpose of the grant is to establish and maintain an epidemiologic surveillance system of selected maternal behaviors a nd experiences before, during, and a Ōer pregnancy. The Department will contract with a survey research ins Ɵtute to collect data through a mailed quesƟonnaire, web-module, and/or a telephone interview and enter the data into a database.
* * *
State Systems Development IniƟaƟve (SSDI) Grant The SSDI grant complements the MCHSBG program by improving the availability, Ɵmeliness, and quality of Maternal and Child Health data. The purpose of this grant is to enhance data capacity by increasing access to and building capabili Ɵes for data collec Ɵon, data analysis, data systems, and linked informaƟon systems. The outcomes of this project will allow for be Ʃer evaluaƟon and measurement of the MCHSBG program goals and objec Ɵves, iden ƟﬁcaƟon of health trends, and improved program planning and management of services, and the development of interim needs assessment acƟviƟes.
* * *
Sudden Unexpected Infant Death (SUID) Case Registry Grant The purpose of the grant is to further the work to idenƟfy prevenƟon strategies related to SUID by improving pracƟces related to collecƟon of comprehensive informaƟon about SUIDs and the development of data-driven best pracƟces and policies that will reduce SUID.
* * *
PrevenƟng Maternal Deaths: SupporƟng Maternal Mortality Review CommiƩees This grant supports the Maternal Mortality Review Program (MMRP), which manages the mulƟdisciplinary Maternal Mortality Review Commi Ʃee (MMRC). The MMRP receives cases of pregnancy-associated deaths, veri ﬁes the deaths, requests records, abstracts the records to create de-idenƟﬁed case summaries, assigns the case summaries to the MMRC for review, and facilitates the MMRC review meeƟngs. The goal of the review meeƟngs is to develop acƟonable recommendaƟons to eliminate preventable pregnancy-associated deaths.
* * *
Maternal Health InnovaƟon Program This grant supports the development of comprehensive, data-driven, and collabora Ɵve maternal health systems with a focus on addressing dispariƟes for populaƟons disproporƟonately impacted by maternal morbidity and mortalit y. Through the Pennsylvania Perinatal Quality CollaboraƟve, Pennsylvania’s Maternal Health Task Force, a mulƟdisciplinary group of members idenƟfy and work to implement strategies to improve the health of women and the systems that provide them care. ## MCH Lead Poisoning & Abatement
The Department receives grants from federal agencies to implement programs related to primary and secondary lead exposure prevenƟon and educaƟon.
* * *
Lead Hazard Control and Healthy Home Programs The Department uses funding from Housin g and Urban Development (HUD) to provide services related to removal and abatement of lead hazards in low-income owner-occupied and rental homes with children. The Healthy Home (HH) supplemental funding is used to provide HH assessments and o ﬀer a variety of environmental and safety interven Ɵons to mi Ɵgate home hazards.
* * *
Childhood Lead Poisoning PrevenƟon Program Using funding from the Centers for Disease Control and PrevenƟon (CDC), the Department works to strengthen blood lead tes Ɵng, reporƟng, and surveillance, linking exposed children to recommended services, and targeted populaƟon-based intervenƟons. The Department provides lead poisoning related educa Ɵon, referrals, and resources to residents of Pennsylvania using a toll-free number.
* * *
Screening Newborns This appropria Ɵon provides funding for the federal share of the cost of screening MA eligible newborns and children in the NSFP.
* * *
Newborn Hearing Screening and IntervenƟon Funding supports Pennsylvania’s Early Hearing Detec Ɵon and Interven Ɵon System of services so that deaf and hard of hearing ne wborns, infants, and young children up to age 3 receive appropriate and Ɵmely services, including hearing screening, diagnosis, early intervenƟon (EI), and family support. The Program also works closely with Family Connec Ɵons for Language and Learning to provide family services and partners with EI through a data share to ensure children with hearing loss are promptly referred and enrolled into EI services.

Disbursement Criteria: Services provided to tuberculosis (TB) patients, those suspected to have TB, contacts of TB patients, and others at high-risk include: anti-tuberculosis medication for treatment and prevention of disease; outpatient examination and diagnostic services; hospitalization for persons with tuberculosis who are very ill, require inpatient care, and have no source of payment; laboratory services; x-ray services, if there is no source of payment; in-field, Directly Observed Therapy for patients to complete recommended therapy; contact examination; provision of preventive therapy to close contacts of infectious cases; and preventive therapy for other high-risk tuberculosis skin test reactors. Disbursements are made based on an hourly rate for wage clinicians, as well as contractual agreements with county and municipal health departments for clinical and treatment services. ## Tuberculosis Screening & Treatment
Tuberculosis (TB) Screening and Treatment services are provided to pa Ɵents with TB, paƟents with suspected TB, persons who are contacts of TB paƟents, and other high-risk persons with no alterna Ɵve source of payment. Services include an Ɵ-tuberculosis medica Ɵons for treatment and prevenƟon of disease; outpaƟent examinaƟon and diagnosƟc services; laboratory services; x-ray services; contact examinaƟon and provision of prevenƟve therapy to close contacts of infecƟous cases; and prevenƟve therapy for paƟents at high risk for developing TB to decrease disease burden and morbidity in the Commonwealt h. The Department’s state health centers, county and municipal health departments, and other contractors provide these services. Funding for TB prevenƟon and treatment acƟviƟes is provided through a combinaƟon of state and federal funds. In addi Ɵon, county and municipal health departments receive funds under the Local Health Administra Ɵon Law (Act 315) to include TB preven Ɵon and treatment services. Currently, all newly diagnosed people with TB are treated using Directly Observed Therapy (DOT), including video DOT within the state health districts. DOT ensures compleƟon of treatment to prevent recurrence and minimizes the risk of a paƟent developing drug-resistant TB. All county and municipal health departments are required to abide by the DOT policy as a contractual requirement for funding. DOT is provided at a locaƟon convenient to the paƟent using a network of regional outreach workers and nursing staﬀ. All paƟents aƩending a TB clinic are pretest-counseled and oﬀered HIV tesƟng. This tesƟng is in accordance with the Centers for Disease Control and Preven Ɵon recommenda Ɵons for paƟents diagnosed with TB or suspected of having TB, and pa Ɵents with latent TB infec Ɵon. TesƟng f or HIV is strongly encouraged at the state-supported TB clinics. TB Program sta ﬀ, nursing staﬀ, and district oﬃce staﬀ provide an ever-increasing role in community educaƟon and support related to TB evalua Ɵon and care. Con Ɵnued educa Ɵon and outreach to private healthcare providers and the public have e ﬀecƟvely reduced community public health concerns. Program staﬀ have developed a comprehensive TB manual to improve TB opera Ɵons. This manual is available to providers throughout the state. The TB Program also facilitates a TB Elimina Ɵon Advisory CommiƩee made up of subject maƩer experts in the ﬁeld of TB. A TB medical consultant chairs this commiƩee.
* * *

## Adult CysƟc Fibrosis and Other Chronic Respiratory Illnesses
CysƟc ﬁbrosis is an autosomal recessive gene Ɵc disorder that impairs the normal clearance of mucus from the lungs. Adults with cys Ɵc ﬁbrosis exhibit increased incidence of diabetes, osteoporosis, liver problems, arthri Ɵs, and gastrointes Ɵnal and pancrea Ɵc issues. Eligible adults with cys Ɵc ﬁbrosis receive the following services: medical evalua Ɵon, treatment, psychosocial support, case management, rehabilitaƟon (including outpaƟent and inpaƟent care), diagnosƟc tests, and laboratory studies. The pharmaceu Ɵcal program is administered by the PharmaceuƟcal Assistance Contract for the Elderly Program. Pulmonologists specializing in adult health care parƟcipate in children’s cysƟc ﬁbrosis clinics to aid and encourage transiƟon to adult care providers. Page 168 of 307Page 168 of 307

Cooley’s Anemia
* * *
Cooley’s anemia is a rare, life-threatening blood disorder that requires regular transfusions and extensive medical care. People with Cooley’s anemia make less hemoglobin and fewer circula Ɵng red blood cells than normal, which re sults in mild or severe anemia. The condiƟon is geneƟcally inherited, and severe symptoms of Cooley’s anemia generally appear by age two. Eligible children and adults with Cooley’s anemia receive the following comprehensive services: medical evalua Ɵon, treatment, psychosocial support, rehabilita Ɵon, voca Ɵonal planning, geneƟc screening, and family counseling. Page 172 of 307Page 172 of 307

Hemophilia
* * *
Hemophilia is a rare inherited blood disorder that causes blood to clot less, which results in an increased risk of bleeding or bruising. E ligible children and adults with hemophilia receive comprehensive medical evaluaƟon, treatment, psychosocial support, rehabilitaƟve services, and blood products. Specialized hemophilia clinics o ﬀer onsite medical evalua Ɵon and treatment, infusion treatments, nutri Ɵonal counseling, physical therapy, and dental evalua Ɵons and treatment. Lupus
* * *
Lupus is a chronic in ﬂammatory condiƟon that aﬀects joints, muscles, skin, kidneys, and other parts of the body. The cause of lupus is s Ɵll unknown. Lupus is more prevalent among women, with symptoms ﬁrst appearing between the ages of 18 to 45. Addi Ɵonally, lupus occurs more oŌen in African Americans than Caucasians. This appropriaƟon provides funds to promote self-management interven Ɵons and programs to help people with lupus and their families manage their disease more eﬀecƟvely, as well as fund research into the eƟology of lupus and new forms of diagnosis and treatment. Sickle Cell
* * *
Sickle cell disease (SCD) is the name given to a group of geneƟc condiƟons that aﬀect the structure of red blood cells. Sickle cell anemia is the most serious form of SCD. These condiƟons are found most o Ōen in the African-American popula Ɵon followed by the Hispanic popula Ɵon. The program provides access to medical and psyc hosocial services for persons diagnosed with SCD. This is accomplished through grants with pediatric and adult sickle cell treatment centers and community-based sickle cell agenci es. Services provided include diagnos Ɵc tes Ɵng, counseling, improving access to quality care, and SCD educaƟon and outreach. Page 186 of 307Page 186 of 307

## Regional Poison Control Centers
This appropriaƟon provides supplemental funding for two regional poison control centers that provide emergency poison informaƟon 24 hours per day, 7 days per week, to residents and visitors to the Commonwealth through a toll-free number. These regional poison control centers also provide research into poison preven Ɵon methodologies and poison informa Ɵon when requested by the public or health care professionals and poison educaƟon programs. ## _71 P.S. § 532_
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
Funding is provided to a qualified grantee in eastern Pennsylvania and a qualified grantee in western Pennsylvania, to provide a continuum of support services, including: a toll-free information and referral helpline, education, support groups, and summer camps. Page 197 of 307Page 197 of 307
* * *
## Epilepsy Support Services
The Epilepsy Support Services Program provides a con Ɵnuum of support services for children, youth, and adults diagnosed with epil epsy or a related seizure disorder and their aﬀected loved ones. Services are oﬀered statewide and include informaƟon and referral via a toll free helpline, client educa Ɵon, client advocacy, support groups, parent-to-parent and peer-to peer linkage, children’s summer camps, and teen retreats. The program also works to educate the community and eliminate the nega Ɵve stereotypes associated with epilepsy through a comprehensive outreach and educa Ɵon program, including: seizure recogni Ɵon and ﬁrst aid training; mass and targeted mailings; employer, provider, and school-based educa Ɵon, conferences, health fairs, and community event parƟcipaƟon; and outreach to family physicians, hospitals, neurologists, and the mental health community. ToureƩe's Syndrome ToureƩe's Syndrome (TS) is a neurological disorder that may cause sudden unwanted or uncontrolle d rapid and repeated movements or vocal sounds called Ɵ cs. The TS program provides a statewide, community-based educaƟon and outreach program for children and adults diagnosed with TS. The program also seeks to idenƟfy children and adults with TS in under-se rved counƟes, as well as minority and culturally diverse communiƟes, and refers these individuals for direct support services. AddiƟonal program services include a toll free telephone helpline/support network, educaƟonal in-service programs, workshops, advocacy, support groups, referral and support services for TS paƟents and their families. ## _35 P.S. sec. 6231 et seq_
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
Act 2014-83 established a Task Force on Lyme Disease and Related Tick-Borne Diseases. This appropriation is used to implement Task Force recommendations regarding prevention, education, and surveillance of Lyme disease. Disbursements are made based on approved invoices. Page 219 of 307Page 219 of 307

## VI. EXPLANATION OF CHANGES APPROPRIATION:
($ Amounts in Thousands) Lyme Disease State $ Federal $ Other $ Total GRANT & SUBSIDY 1. To continue surveillance and prevention activities: $2,000 $0 $0 $2,000 Subtotal Grant & Subsidy $2,000 $0 $0 $2,000 BUDGETARY RESERVE 1. Change in Budgetary Reserve: ($2,000) $0 $0 ($2,000) Subtotal Budgetary Reserve ($2,000) $0 $0 ($2,000) TOTAL $0 $0 $0 $0 Page 220 of 307Page 220 of 307
* * *
Lyme Disease
* * *
The Lyme Disease PrevenƟon Program implements recommendaƟons from the 2022 Lyme and Other Tickborne Diseases Interagency Workgroup Report, focusing on recommendaƟons to educate and build awareness among the public and healthcare professionals. Intended outcomes of the program include: • Increase knowledge among the general populaƟon regarding Lyme disease prevenƟon methods and strategies. • Increase knowledge among healthcare professionals regarding Lyme disease prevenƟon, diagnosis, and reporƟng to the Department.
* * *
Emphasis is dedicated to surveillance acƟviƟes, including: • Increase the understanding of the Ɵck populaƟon in Pennsylvania through Department of Environmental ProtecƟon (DEP) Ɵck surveillance. Adult and nymphal Ɵcks of all species are collected and tested for pathogens. The emerging Haemophysalis longicornis Ɵcks have been collected each year and tested for mulƟple pathogens. DEP idenƟﬁed a new Ɵck species to Pennsylvania, Amblyomma maculatum which was not known to have established colonies as far north as Pennsylvania. CDC assisted with tesƟng this Ɵck species for RickeƩsia parkeri. DEP also collects and monitors Ɵck populaƟons of Amblyomma americanum which can transmit ehrlichiosis, Heartland and Bourbon viruses, and has been linked to alpha-gal allergy syndrome. • Provide funding to the Department of ConservaƟon and Natural Resources (DCNR) for Ɵck educaƟon and Ɵck miƟgaƟon in state parks. The funding provided to DCNR enabled them to remove Ɵck habitats in state parks, making them safer for visitors. This is an ongoing acƟvity. DCNR employees also provide Ɵck educaƟon in state parks to visitors as needed. • Pr ovide funding to the Pennsylvania Department of Agriculture (DOA) to conduct Ɵck educaƟon for farms and other stakeholders. DOA also conducts Ɵck tesƟng from surveillance conducted at farms to idenƟfy Ɵck species and pathogens that may be of concern. • Provide funding to other state agencies such as Fish and Game and Pennsylvania Department of TransportaƟon to allow them to provide Ɵck prevenƟon materials to their outdoor employees such as repellent and permethrin treated clothing. • Improve tradiƟonal surveillance informaƟon on Lyme through enhanced interviews of a porƟon of Lyme cases. Enhanced interviews were completed on a subset of 2019 Lyme cases and a manuscript on the ﬁndings is being prepared for publicaƟon. A ﬁnal report will be available to the public in 2025. Page 221 of 307Page 221 of 307
* * *
• Improve newer surveillance techniques through enhanced use of syndromic surveillance. Syndromic surveillance data is published on the Department’s Ɵckborne diseases website. • Increase knowledge among the general populaƟon to build awareness of prevenƟve steps to avoid Ɵcks, steps to reduce Ɵck environments around the home, and what to do when you ﬁnd a Ɵck on you or your family member.
* * *
Materials were released to educate school age children on Ɵcks and Lyme. A pilot program was conducted in six high-incidence school districts in which a Ɵck and Lyme disease safety program was administered to fourth graders. EvaluaƟons were analyzed and signiﬁcant knowledge improvements were found for all evaluaƟon quesƟons and some improvements in increased use of insect repellent were noted. The data weas presented at a naƟonal conference in 2023 and the vector-borne disease team conducted train-the-trainer sessions in three regions of Pennsylvania to educators so they may provide Ɵck and Lyme educaƟon in their own schools. A Ɵck safety escape room is in development. This is targeted at older school age children and can be used in classrooms, scouƟng troops, and camps.
* * *
Camp vector safety materials were created and released on the Department’s website. The camp booklet provides educaƟon on Ɵcks, mosquitoes, vector-borne illnesses, and prevenƟon tools. Guidance is provided to camps on vector bite miƟgaƟon and signs and symptoms of vector-borne diseases. A checklist was also created to help parents and guardians determine how to prevent vector bites at camp.
* * *
EducaƟng health care professionals (HCPs) will bring the health care community up to date with rapidly evolving science, the associated risks of exposure, what to do about bites and early stages of disease, and the importance of early diagnosis and of reporƟng cases of Lyme and other Ɵck-borne diseases. A provider training and educaƟon module was released in 2019 to improve understanding and idenƟﬁcaƟon of overall Ɵckborne diseases, discuss the Department’s role in prevenƟon and surveillance for Ɵckborne diseases, improve provider re porƟng, and provide informaƟon on current best pracƟces for treatment. The provider educaƟon is available to all health care workers pracƟcing in Pennsylvania. QuesƟon and answer documents for HCPs on Lyme disease and anaplasmosis were released in 2022. In 2024, an HCP survey was administered to beƩer understand knowledge gaps. The Lyme disease coordinator will work with Penn State University to conduct further analysis of HCP Ɵck and Lyme disease knowledge and to idenƟfy the best messaging strategies for HCPs. During late 2025 through 2026, the Lyme disease coordinator and the public health educator will develop materials on anƟbioƟc stewardship regarding Ɵckborne disease to disseminate to HCPs. Inappropriate use of anƟbioƟcs for Ɵck bites and Ɵckborne diseases has been idenƟﬁed as an area of concern, therefore, the Department will provide addiƟonal resources to HCPs to address this issue. Page 222 of 307Page 222 of 307
* * *
In 2023, the Department engaged a media company to conduct a statewide media campaign to alert people in Pennsylvania about the risks of Ɵcks. Approximately 180 million impressions were delivered to people residing in and visiƟng Pennsylvania. In 2025, the same company was contracted to conduct a smaller Ɵck safety awareness campaign in Pennsylvania.
* * *
In 2023, the Department released a series of ﬁve educaƟonal videos on YouTube and on their website to educate the public on Ɵcks and Lyme disease. The videos were edited to shorter lengths and provided to Pennsylvania Driver and Vehicle Services to air on monitors in locaƟons throughout the state.
* * *
In 2023, the Department hired an intern with federal funds to conduct a preliminary surveillance study on alpha-gal allergy syndrome (AGS). The intern interviewed people in PA who had tested posiƟve for AGS to beƩer understand their symptoms, foods that caused the symptoms, onset of symptoms, and Ɵck bite history. In 2025, the Department will be requesƟng that labs that test for AGS voluntarily send posiƟve reports to the Department and interviews will be conducted by foodborne disease interns.
* * *
The Department’s Bureau of Epidemiology (BOE) has worked with public health educators to develop Ɵck and Ɵckborne disease educaƟonal materials for the public in mulƟple languages. The materials are distributed at numerous events throughout the state.
* * *
The BOE provided Ɵck prevenƟon materials to growers throughout the state for employees who may be at risk for Ɵck bites. The growers were instructed to set up vector prevenƟon staƟons on their farms so that employees could apply permethrin to their shoes and insect repellent to themselves at work. In 2024, 11 growers requested the materials; in 2025, 28 growers requested materials.
* * *
Working with other agencies and with providers will also serve to generally increase messaging on prevenƟon approaches, overall awareness of Lyme disease, and improve access to early and appropriate treatment, all of which are idenƟﬁed within the intent of Act 83 of 2014. Page 223 of 307Page 223 of 307

## Emergency Medical Services
The purpose of the Emergency Medical Services (EMS) Act is to initiate, maintain, and improve the emergency medical services system in the Commonwealth, thereby preventing and reducing the mortality and morbidity rate of individuals requiring unexpected medical care in life threatening incidents.
* * *
The Emergency Medical Services Operating Fund (EMSOF) supports EMS program activities through contracts with 13 regional EMS councils and a state advisory council. The regional EMS councils conduct education, process certiﬁcations, coordinate communicatio ns projects, inspect ambulance services, distribute ambulance equipment funds, collect data, accomplish activities related to all- hazard preparedness and response, and generally assist the Department in coordinating the state EMS system. Funding is available to provide prehospital provider equipment, administrative support of the regional EMS councils, instructional costs for prehospital educational programs, public information and education, quality assurance, data collection and information, ambulance licensure, medical command facility accreditation, coordination of EMS activities with the 54 accredited trauma centers in the Commonwealth, and improvement of telecommunications systems. Page 233 of 307Page 233 of 307
* * *

## _35 P.S. § 6935 (e); The act of July 23, 2020, P.L. 670, No. 69; The act of October 29,2020, P.L. 773, No. 93._
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
This appropriation supports post-acute head injury rehabilitation services for residents who have experienced a traumatic head injury after July 3, 1985, and have exhausted alternative financial resources. Services are provided in residential facilities, day (outpatient) facilities, or home and community-based settings. Head injury services are delivered through Participating Provider Agreements with head injury rehabilitation facilities. Effective with Act 69 of 2020, this appropriation also funds a contractual agreement for a first responder statewide critical incident stress management program. Page 236 of 307Page 236 of 307
* * *

## Catastrophic Medical and Rehabilitation
The Head Injury Program (HIP) was created in 1988 by the Emergency Medical Services Act of 1985 and provides post -acute head injury rehabilitation services to residents who have experienced a traumatic head injury after July 3, 1985, and have exhausted alternative ﬁnancial resources. The goal of the HIP is to address the social, cognitive, behavioral, and physical needs of these individuals so they can live and function independently in their homes and communities. Services are provided in residential facilities, day (outpatient) facilities, or home- and community based settings. Head injury services are delivered through Participating Provider Agreements with head injury rehabilitation facilities. Regulations for the operation of the Head Injury Program were published in the Pennsylvania Bulletin and became eﬀective August 27, 2001. These regulations established time and funding limits for client services. Rehabilitation services focus on enabling clients to progress to a higher level of functioning and to transition to less restrictive environments.
* * *
Pre-enrollment assistance is oﬀered to applicants. This service assists clients and their families with the DOH application process and with accessing a variety of brain injury services across state agencies.
* * *
Act 69 of 2020 established the First Responder Statewide Critical Incident Stress Management Program, which identiﬁes the emotional impact that external and internal critical incidents have on Commonwealth emergency responders; prepares responses to event -driven situations aﬀecting the emotional well -being of emergency responders and updates the Critical Incident Stress Management Team level participation in the Pennsylvania Voluntary Critical Incident Stress Management Network. The Act required the department develop a program of trauma and suicide awareness and impact training as well as require this training be included as a component of initial and continuing education for EMS providers and be made available to other emergency responders. Up to $250,000 for this program is to be provided from funds identiﬁed for Catastrophic Medical and Rehabilitation. Page 238 of 307Page 238 of 307
* * *

## _20 Pa. C.S.A § 8621; 8622_
Disbursement Criteria:
* * *
The Governor Casey Organ and Tissue Donation Awareness Fund was established by Act 102 of 1994 and derives revenue from private contributions and a voluntary add-on to the fee for an original or renewal driver's license, state identification card or vehicle registration. Act 90 of 2018 increased the voluntary add-on amount from $1 to $3. This fund pays for the departmental operating costs associated with the Fund and supports the Organ Donation Advisory Committee. Funding distributions are based on salary and benefit requirements for authorized complement as well as invoices for operating expenses. Page 246 of 307Page 246 of 307

* * *
The Governor Robert P. Casey Memorial Organ and Tissue Donation Awareness Trust Fund was established by Act 102 of 1994. The Fund derives income from private contributions, voluntary deductions from individual state income tax refunds, a voluntary add- on f ee for a driver’s license or state identiﬁcation card, and a voluntary add-on fee for a vehicle registration. Act 90 of 2018 increased the voluntary add-on fee for driver’s license/state identiﬁcation card and vehicle registration from $1 to $3. Funding is used in coordination with the statewide public awareness program conducted by certiﬁed Organ Procurement Organizations to encourage Pennsylvanians to become organ and tissue donors. ## Patient Financial Hardship Program
This appropriation provides funding for medical marijuana patients who demonstrate ﬁnancial hardship or need under Section 902 of Act 16 of 2016 (35 P.S. Section 10231.101 10231.2110), amended by Act 44 of 2021 (P.L. 201, No. 44), herein referred to as the Act. Through this appropriation, the department has implemented the Medical Marijuana Assistance Program (MMAP) to ensure maximum availability to individuals with ﬁnancial need. MMAP waives the cost of an identiﬁcation card under sections 501(c)(5) and 502(a)(2) of the Act for eligible medical marijuana patients and caregivers; eliminates the cost of background checks for caregivers; and oﬀers a monthly ﬁnancial beneﬁt to eligible medical marijuana patients to purchase medical marijuana products at a dispensary, as determined by available funding. The Bureau of Medical Marijuana initiated the monthly ﬁnancial beneﬁt in the form of a pilot program, to medical marijuana patients who participate in the Department of Aging’s PACE/PACENET program. Currently, each eligible medical marijuana patient receives a monthly ﬁnancial beneﬁt of $50 that can be used to purchase any forms of medication permitted under their medical marijuana patient certiﬁcation. ## Health Research – Health Priorities
Act 2001-77 authorized the Department to establish a health research program called the Commonwealth Universal Research Enhancement and allocates funds from the tobacco settlement fund for broad- based health research. The Health Research Program oversees the awarding of broad-based health research grants to Pennsylvania-based researchers, universities, medical schools, and other institutions. Research projects may focus on basic biomedical research, patient-oriented clinical investigations, and health services research. Health services research includes studies related to the delivery of health care services as well as research designed to promote and maintain health, prevent disease, and translate research advances into community health care practice. Seventy percent of funds are awarded based on a formula calculated using the institution’s average award from the National Institutes of Health for the three previous years. Unless speciﬁcally addressed in the annual ﬁscal code, the Department determines priorities with the Health Research Advisory Committee. The committee meets at least twice a year to provide advice and recommendations on research priorities, grant account ability, evaluation procedures, and other issues the Health Research Program puts before them. Formula funded research priorities must include the identiﬁcation of critical research areas, disparities in health status among various populations, expected research outcomes and beneﬁts and disease prevention and treatment methodologies. The goal of the research should be to improve health status and access for Pennsylvanians. Through the application process and accountability requirements, the Department encourages research that emphasizes collaboration, promotes business and community involvement, increases infrastructure and research capacity, increases the number of new investigators, new grants, new discoveries, and new products, leverages new and existing research funds, and leads to population- based applications that address disparities in health status. All research grants are statutorily required to be completed within a four -year period. The request for applications for formula grants is issued each year after the Department completes the certiﬁcation and eligibility process and grantees conﬁrm federal grant award levels. Act 2001-77 provides for an Ethics Advisory Board of six individuals that shall be convened by the Secretary to advise and make recommendations “when a research project may be denied due to ethical considerations.” Funding shall be denied for a project “based on a ﬁnding of improper ethical considerations by a majority of the board.” Because the Act prohibits Board members from being aﬃliated with an applicant whose grant proposal is under review, the Department intends to establish a new Board each time a Board opinion is required. All grantees submit annual reports by July 31 of each year and a ﬁnal progress report at the end of the grant. An annual report on all research funded during the prior state ﬁscal year is provided to the General Assembly and placed on the Department’s we bsite under the Tobacco Settlement/Act 77 link for the Commonwealth Universal Research Enhancement Program. Performance reviews are conducted to evaluate the eﬀectiveness of each research project funded by a grant. Page 285 of 307Page 285 of 307
* * *

## Health Research – National Cancer Institute
Act 77 of 2001, the Tobacco Settlement Act, authorizes the Pennsylvania Department of Health to establish a health research program called the Commonwealth Universal Research Enhancement (CURE). The CURE allocated one percent of the tobacco settlement fund s to institutions that received National Cancer Institute (NCI) funding. All of the institutions eligible for health research formula funds, based on NCI grant funding, are also eligible for health research formula funds based on grants received from the National Institute of Health (NIH). Institutions eligible for the health research formula funds (either NCI/NIH or NIH only) submit a grant application to the Department. After the applications are processed, funds are awarded for research projects that are statutorily required to be completed within four years. Page 290 of 307Page 290 of 307
* * *
